Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes, it is swollen and full of pus and corrupt matter, you must probe it thoroughly with great subtlety, and make sure you know its depth entirely. After cleaning the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the size of the cavity, and continue burning until the surrounding flesh and matter are burnt away, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the extent of the wound; beware not to burn the nerves nearby and large veins. If the fistula goes towards the body of the bladder and the intestines, be careful with these areas, and do not act elsewhere except in charnut, and think that it is not persistent; afterwards cure the area until it is healed, if the area is sealed and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is healed entirely; but if the matter has not been removed, then know that the area is open, and the bone is corrupted at the spot; and thus as one of those we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of cold comes to the kidneys and of large swelling, and it does not take on female form, then it is necessary that you perform cautery over the kidneys from both sides with the clavicle cautery as we have previously said; and if we cauterize in milk, it will have four cauteries in line, and it will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft due to cold or moisture, and the patient retains urine, then make a fire cautery in the area outside the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right side and one on the left side, and both should be as long as the little finger; and make one incision behind the back, or two if needed; and the incisions should be parallel to each other according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	of the kidney
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidney is cold and moist and cannot conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their term is delayed; and when they come, it causes great pain: then you must make four cauteries around the belly, as we have said in the caution of the bladder, and two cauteries behind the back; and the incisions should be parallel to each other, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the wound
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors sink into the wound of the thigh, and for this reason it becomes silent from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints of the limb are found to be separated, if you must cauterize the patient on the wound of the thigh with .i. cautery resembling a circle, and sign in front of the joint around the wound so that the wound is within the circle; and if the cauteries are like those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make four large olive-shaped cauteries, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the others; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the haunch
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hollow of the haunch, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated as we have said in the division but the cure is of no use, and the illness is old: therefore you must purge the patient from the large humors with fetid pills or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After this, you make the cautery; and the method of the cautery is according to two methods: either with burning substances, or fire cautery. The fire cautery is according to many ways, one of which is as follows: you perform four triangular cauteries on the hollow of the haunch, and make a good depth and width, and have space between each cautery the size of a die, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is performed in the middle on the top of the haunch, so there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, cauterize the circular cautery in the dislocation of the shoulder blade; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire shoulder blade, and all the edges of the wound are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And it is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain is in the shoulder blade and does not reach the thigh nor the leg. And if it comes to the thigh and the leg, two cauteries should be applied where the patient says that the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle .4 fingers, on the left side a little bit; and let the cauteries be cutleries, and burn the edge of the wound; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the foot or near it, cauterize where he feels the pain with 2 or 4 points, which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, do more; and if the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, apply a cautery with a cutlery or circular tool, but be careful in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery too much so as to burn nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who made a fire cautery on the ankle bone, and they let it be for so long that the leg became completely swollen, and the foot also, and all the toes were pierced and corrupted. After a belly purge of which they died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery in one and the other, according to this method. // The wise will say about the hock cautery, here is how it is done, make a nail of such size as a small finger's joint or slightly smaller, and be perpendicular or diagonal between each other at a distance equal to the diameter of a nut, and the distance between each should be two fingers apart, and they should be round like nuts, and there should be one handle of iron well made; this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it up until it becomes completely red and boiling hot, and then put it on the ill ankle, turning it towards the healthy side; and cauterize once with a single cautery and let it rest for four days. Then apply plaster made of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this fire cautery due to its fearsome aspect, and few know how to use it effectively; however, it is one of the good cauteries, which can be endured by those who can, and where it can be applied.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether it be from falling or impact or too much evacuation, or like the effects of cold matter spreading, none of these symptoms call for cauteries, except in the case of cold matter infusion.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after this, that the patient be emptied of foul pills or similar things, which are to be placed on the back, where the pain is felt, three lines marked with ink, and in each line 5 or more cauteries according to the strength and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and the cautery should be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do 4 cauteries or 2 according to the medium-sized cautery in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Often this disease comes to small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a narrow anus when they become constipated, and fear; and you find in the lower spine on the back and in our appearance which appears above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it with the cautery of this shape.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	The first sentence to translate is: "The fire cautery increases each part of the spine. If you see, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing 2 or 3 lines, and let the tips be close to each other. After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, ensure that you do not administer cautery in a gumboil that is in nerve spasm."
de la dolor des jointes	"of the pain of the joints"
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	"When the pain of the joints is due to moisture that has spread throughout all members of the body and when the pain occurs in the feet, which are called "podagre" properly, and when it is from cold causes and medicines cannot cure it, it is treated with cauteries as follows: make a hot iron cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:"
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary for you to prick the face of the foot, make a fire cautery all over the cautery called "point". And if pain comes up to the knees and other joints, and this often happens, make a fire cautery on each knee four times or four in each part, all over the olive oil cautery; and if more is needed, do more, but do not hold your hand too long until the fat of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pain descends to the knees and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. If the pain is in the hands, do pricks around the wrist two lines; if there remains no more pain in the fingers, do pricks on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and think about medicines. For if you take good care of him and purge the fever, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	The dislocation of the shoulder joint due to moisture can be treated by resetting it. If it repeatedly dislocates with slight movement, you must first reset the dislocation. When resetting a dislocation, the head of the humerus bone should be pushed back into its socket. This treatment is also known as reduction of the shoulder joint.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When eruptions come in anger, and the bowels descend to the kidneys and this is new, it is necessary that when you wish to cure it, you must not let him eat that day; and he should use things which relax the stomach, so that the feces descend from his stomach; afterwards have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his flank as long as the bowels are repaired, and hold them at your sides, and sign with a mark like half of a circle above the abdomen; then heat the cautery in the shape as shown here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	And let it be white and let him pass stools. Then move the bowels back to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so they do not return; and work well the thighs on the patient, and put one cushion and one sergeant on the thighs, and another one under him who holds his hands; then put the cautery over the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bowels do not burst when you make the cautery; and that you do not burn him; and that by these means the patient does not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. It is necessary that the cauteries for children are subtle according to their size, and those of adults also large according to their size; after three days, cure the wound caused by the cautery with butter so that the burn is removed; after that, cure other medicines until he is well, and lay the patient for forty days on his back so that the wound heals well; it is necessary that his bedding be left long, so that the bowels do not burst when he gets up to go to his chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when it wants to rise, bring a well-made bandage and keep it for another 40 days; let him have good rest, so that he should work little and take care not to fill too much with drinking and eating, and not to raise too much voice; and when he follows this teaching, he will be completely healthy. And I shall say afterwards the cure of amputation in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the wound from the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When the wounds occur in other bellies and are known to not grow more, make one cautery of the right size according to its quantity and let it be burned one-third of the skin; after that cure as we have said; and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized at four angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first mark the joint with ink and draw a line over the dislocation site, and another one away from it. Then place your hand on top of the entire cautery. However, the first cauteries are easier and more manageable.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, whether it is from a fall or injury, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the medicine does not cure it, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb, its smallness, weakness, and nature, as well as its location in terms of twisting and pain. If it is healed by the first cautery, that's good; if not, start another one immediately on top of the first, for custom dictates that the cauteries should move to the nearest limb until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	To mix (or compound) medicine
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The mixing of medicine is sometimes greatly aided by the use of cautery, and especially so for those who suffer from illness arising from putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. If you see it being cauterized, take care that the illness is in its early stages, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or linger, then perform five cauteries on the head: one at the nape of the neck, another near the front at the end of the hair; two at each temple; and one behind the ear; leave your hand long enough for the cautery to reach the bone, and so that the scorch marks come out beyond the skin so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize over the mice according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the medicine has spread all over, it will surely disappear, then you must cauterize with those cauteries we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery at the nape of the neck, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one at the buttock and another under it, and two on each shoulder; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the legs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and over the hollows of the hands; be careful not to burn the nerves that are above the lower back, and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more cautery you do, the more help it provides and benefits [the patient]; and know that the sick do not feel pain during cauterization as the healthy do, because the body is already completely corrupted. The cautery should be large or small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the art of ironwork. Afterward, clean the wound with flour several times with honey and other remedies until it heals.
de enfleure	Cauterize the wound with a hot iron.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When inflammation appears in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters but is not healed, then cauterize the affected member according to its size and shape; and let the cautery be a little deeper than the thickness of the skin. Then cure it with ointments until it heals. Sometimes a cauterization is done on the hand, foot, or back, at the site of the nerve that immobilizes the limb, and in this way the inflammation is removed; but let no one interfere unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the movement of the nerves in the body.
de albaras	From the linen cloth [or fabric]
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is recognized, and the instruments of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a shallow cautery, according to the thickness of the skin involved, until the blister is removed and the color changes; then cure it with flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, as well as pig's blood and goose blood, each in equal parts; mix everything together and bind it with a cloth; apply it to the location until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	treating canker with cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a boil first appears and you want to stop it, you should cauterize with the cautery that resembles a circle around the boil's circumference. Although some wise men say to cauterize in the middle of the boil; however, this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen once; and a more proper thing is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circule," as we have said in terms of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot grow
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," which grows slowly due to excess or because the patient is aged (meaning very old) and has little blood, or because of the time; and you want it to grow faster: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking it; afterwards, let it be. For it will hasten to grow.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced entirely with the fire cautery, heat the cautery as shown here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Place your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the boil, and make sure that the cautery is such that the patient feels it burning in this way so that the course of the pus is clear. Afterward, cure it completely when it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another form of illness is called "corrodens," and it is nothing but a consumption of the limb, because it consumes the limbs just like fire dries out damp wood. If you see this disease in a place where it can be cauterized with fire, then heat the cautery to a small and large size, according to the location or the site of the illness; after the cauterization of all parts until you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, that everything that is corrupted is removed. Then leave it for four days, and put soft soothing cauterized broth on the affected areas with oil until the burns caused by the fire are healed, and all the corruption is gone. After the cure with ointments generates healthy skin. And if you see after four days that healthy skin does not grow, it's good; but if this doesn't happen, start cauterizing again on the remaining corrupted parts. And this consumption has sometimes been cured with hot medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already mentioned the cure for hot medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The coming pricks to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	It often happens that a disease called "clos" comes to the feet, which is a large, hard blister that pricks the foot. And the cauteries of this disease are in two ways: fire cautery and hot water cautery. The fire cautery is as follows: you heat one cauterizer like a feather from a raven's wing, made of good iron to the size that can penetrate the nail from all sides, and it should have subtle edges; after heating it very hot on the nail, hold your hand all around the nail until it reaches the nail bed; and leave it for three days until pus begins to come out; then make a plaster of coarse herbs ground with oil, and leave the plaster over the entire area all night, and the cauterizer will dry and be pulled out by its roots. Then heal the wound with soothing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	If the body is turned inside out by an external injury, which often happens in hands and feet, you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done as follows: take a catheter of raven or iron, or a feather from a raven's wing, and place it on the nail and hold it, that is to say, pricks the blisters; then place the catheter so that it surrounds it completely, then put a little hot water, and keep your hand firm, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the catheter reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep to the root; and let the patient suffer a little biting by the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will dry out all its roots. Do this repeatedly until you heal all those that are in the body, then treat them with ointments that soothe the pain.
li cure dou trembler	The Cure for Shaking (or Trembling)
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	For anyone who shakes due to coldness of the nerves, or quartan fever or another, you should apply four or five cauteries on the spinal column between each spine; one cautery in the buttocks and one on the stomach using an olive oil cautery; this will stop the shaking and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of putrid pustules (or boils)
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes, pustules that are putrid and come from large corrupted matter appear on the outside of the body. In such a case, at first when they appear, it is necessary to apply a cautery on top of each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made of myrtle stick or a long root of aristolochia, or a cautery with a lentil shape. Sometimes, they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear in this way, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluous matter that comes from them is discharged, and they become healthy; however, it should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great evacuations of blood from the cut artery in the wound that appears on the surface or at the incision of an abscess or the cauterization of a member, and similar things; it is a very serious matter to bleed out.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	However, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound vein and hold it very tight until the blood is stopped flowing; then apply the olive oil cauterizer (smaller or larger) as many times as necessary until it is all red; next take .i., either large or small depending on the size of the wound and the location in which the artery is severed, and place the cauterizer on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cauterizer there until the bleeding has been stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a jump occurs when you place your hand on the vein, and the fire cautery is extinguished, take immediately another cautery that is near the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	Continue to do this one after the other until the vein is closed; and beware not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and let no further harm come upon the patient; know that when blood stops flowing from the artery, it cannot be properly stopped when the artery is large unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated beforehand, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on it that can stop the blood; and let it be tied and constricted accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the constriction of a narrow ligature or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit if it does not help.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone who has neither sight nor medicine at hand, he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it remains swollen above the wound and the vein; and he must not move it, but the cold moisture should often be applied so that it becomes very cold until the wound is frozen and thickened and remains swollen; and make inquiries in advance for the cauteries and medicines needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgeries (or heals)
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we explained the origins and instruments and forms of cauteries; I placed that chapter on the head to the feet, and I will proceed with this chapter in the same way because those things are easier to understand when they are presented in order.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of this, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to engage in folly. For many ways of people come to treatment. Those who are so ailing with their disease that they die easily from the stupidity they find due to their illness, and from the great cruelty of its malice; and one should have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of those who give you their advice, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the patient is contemptuous. It is not advisable that you should consent to these who come to you who have this manner, but place more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not reveal carelessly but wisely of those about which you are certain, and from which you can take and learn; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients to whom salvation is converted; and this will help you acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, come.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Moreover, I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into sections, according to that which is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have explained from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand those matters from which you will need assistance.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children during birth, and when the head of the child is pressed too hard; and sometimes it happens due to a reason that we are not aware of.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone but children, and for all those I have seen, death was swift; therefore, it seems to me that it is worthwhile to stop the work in some treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and it swelled each day until it could no longer support it; and the moisture collected under the skull between the brain and the bone; and the treatments are such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a large incision in the head; and let it be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture flows out; and here is the form of the lancet:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see the fissures of the head are opened on each side, and they do not respond when you press them from within, then it is necessary that you make four cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then remove the moisture entirely from outside. Afterwards strain the cuts with linen and powder, and put vinegar and oil, and leave it in this condition until the fifth day; then unbind, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head swell gradually, and give the patient dried meat of a moist animal as long as the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incising is that you examine the size of the abscess, and gather the pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then make the incision according to what you can, and be careful not to cut the artery; and let some blood flow out, so that the patient dies a proper death due to blood loss and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of remedy
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone with a disease called "catarrah" in the eyes or at its worst, and the disease is old, and medicine does not help, then the last cure is the cautery on the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them (the arteries), you should have the patient lean back; then rub his neck with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then tighten the patient's collar with one cloth; then look where the veins are, and the heads of the left and right ones are behind the ears, and they are tied down; then mark the heads of incision, then cut each one with a sharp spatula of two parts until the incision reaches the bone, but through the wide neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it (the artery), push the sharp spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting as you would through two.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it jumps up without ceasing continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when touched, you must measure the space of three fingers, then make an incision up to the bone; and the amount of blood that should be allowed to come out is 7 cubits [cubic inches], approximately a little more or less, depending on what the patient can tolerate, and the filling of the artery. Then examine the wound: if it remains above the bone without swelling, if the cut that is incised does not cause an abscess, then hold the wound closed and tie it up, and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of emigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old emigration comes and acute catarrh arrives, due to the moisture of tears and the heat in the temples, and an old foolish person becomes senile with similar things; it is treated by methods of medicine, but it does not help at all. If the arteries in the temples are opened and cauterized, as we have mentioned, it will help.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient pulls back the hairs at the base of his temples, and listens to the opening artery in the temple because it opens well through beating. It can be easily found except in some cold men. If it is found, the patient strains its neck with some cloth, then rubs the place with a rough cloth and moistens the place with hot water until the arteries appear clearly; then take the spatula of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you find the artery, then pull it up to the tweezers and remove all the tissues that are under each side. If the artery is thin, turn it at the tip of the scissors, then cut from that side according to the size of the two shoulders. For if it is not cut, it will not come out entirely without difficulty.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the .vj. c/, up to .iij.; and if the arteries are large, it is necessary that you tie it with a double strong silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound is closed and bleeding stops; then cut off the excess between the two ligatures at that same hour, and if you see fit, cauterize the wound with the cautery knife up to the bone until the pieces are cut through; and this is the moveable work, if the patient does not have fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries are aid for finishing the injuries: which is of greater help to the injured.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary that one fill the area with old cotton and put a well-made tourniquet on top; and when you loosen them, cure it with dry medicines that cause charring, and with tourniquets, until it is healed; and if without the incision of the artery as much as you work, you hurry to cover it by cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze your hand so that the wound does not bleed; and if this is not present, put your hand on the area until it freezes, and rub the area with cold water until it stops bleeding, and squeeze as necessary; and the moveable and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this sharp cautery knife, but the cuts should be well spaced to keep the heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the thermometer is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should be between two knuckles, one of which is thicker in space, and when you have inserted it into the vein by two leagues, and you heat the iron hot until it reaches the bone, and then cut the vein in two leagues; and they should be spaced between two joints because it is not always welded with this cautery all over; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes run down the veins that are above the head of the face and medicine treatment does not help it, and you see the patient frowning, and notice his forehead trembling like shivers; and if they are tender and moist so that the eyelashes fall out, and the eyelids are scalded by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it the ancient "contused cure", and you will do to the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on his forehead, then you will make 3 cuts or evenly on the forehead according to the length of the forehead; one of the cuts shall be as two fingers all along the forehead below, and the others 2 at 2 costal zones above the eyelids, and watch out for the incision of the arteries that are at the 2 costal zones above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the 2 jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of 3 fingers joined.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much linen to wipe the blood, then insert the sharp spatula of 2 parts as shown here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	The first incision is made from the temple down to the second incision; and peel off all the cartilage that is between the two cuts on top of the bone, then proceed from the middle incision down to the other second, and pull out this spatula-like instrument.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the instrument called "cultellaire" in the first incision; it is well sharpened on one side, and on the other side it is soft, not sharp, and it has this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place the cutting edge of the instrument towards the cartilage and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision. Cut all the tendons that descend from the head to the hairs as long as the incision is continuous up to where the cartilage opens, then proceed in the middle incision down to the other opening; and then press equally on the blood and express the liquid for the blood taken; then place a piece of old cotton fabric in each incision, put moistened linen cloths soaked in wine and oil and honey on top, and make sure no pus comes out; on the third day undo the suture, and apply a large amount of cold water, then treat with ointment made of basilicon and rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a sharp catarrh usually comes, and you see the hairs becoming thin and small, and the vision becomes dimmed, and paper burnt; and the hair falls out, and the head aches with acute pain, and the patient coughs; then know by these symptoms that those materials and this catarrh do not come from just one vein, but several. And the cure that is to be made if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you instruct the patient to lean back their head, then make a large cut across the forehead and another along its length. [This means to cut from one temple to the other across the forehead.] Let your hand be far enough away from the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then insert cotton soaked in vinegar and oil between the two sides of the cut, and tie linen over it. Then place damp cloths on it and beware of hot abscesses; when it has been removed, you must rub the bone until char begins to grow, then treat with things that promote the growth of char.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour, and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster with them; administer it in these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	for the draining of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, animals, stones or similar things like iron; seeds, such as peas, beans or lentils; or flowing things such as water and silks and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear stone or some other thing that does not fit in the ear, nor enters into the ear, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, distill a little of violet oil or camphor oil, then apply extraction; and make him sneeze with powders, and stop up the nostrils when sneezing comes, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and stretch the ear upwards. Often times pus comes from this cure; and if it does not come out, apply extraction with fine tweezers, as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with tweezers, that is good; if not, apply extraction with fine and slender onion or a needle, and if it does not come out by this means, make a cane from beeswax and push the head of the cane or ear tube deeply into the ear so that nothing can enter with the cane; then pull it out forcefully, as often times pus comes in this way; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take glue of whatever kind you have on hand, and place it around an instrument suitable for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatnot, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not jump out with all these things we have said, you should hurry to incise the ear before an abscess comes, and spasm occurs; and the method of incision is that you first cleanse the patient's head and draw blood according to the measure of its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat or the place it depends on; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it immediately into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is swollen and growing, administer extraction; and if it cannot be drained, administer a thin and fine probe according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	If it is swollen and growing, make an incision of that swelling. But do not do this if you think the swelling is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made several cuts; then extract it with fine pliers dipped in vinegar or wine, as we have said, so that the extraction is straight.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In water that drips into the ear, the patient should use warm compresses of early herbs and stuff the ear with cotton. Let it lie on that ear itself or let the water fall out if it jumps. If it does not jump, take several thin and light stones according to the length of your finger and heat one slightly in the fire; put a piece of cloth or linen from the ear into the patient's mouth, and strike one stone against another on the stone in the ear, and hit with another stone on the striking stone; keep doing this with one stone against another until the water jumps out completely, and then it will jump out entirely; and if you see, take a feather and push one end into the ear, and take hold of the other end of the feather with fire until the outermost feather is burned; then repeat this with other feathers until the water jumps out completely, as we have said in the earlier section.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of small animals, like fleas and similar things, treat them as we have said in the division; but if they are large and can be felt, bring tools for extraction such as tweezers; and it is easier to remove what is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earwigs, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in treating with distillations, it does not help; if there are no worms present, take the thread of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	Make it narrow on one side and wide on the other. Insert the most subtle end into the ear according to the degree of suffering of the patient, then grasp the whole string; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey, stop up around the string with cotton as I have said in the previous chapter; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in removing earwigs, and you will find them or treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this device as you see here:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make a container of silver or tin placed below one small hole, and above it cover with a distiller; and for pressing within the distillation have one device made of tin well-made for this purpose, and if you see take one scraper and wind around its tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you wish in the container, and let it be in the ear; then push down into the scraper with all the cotton and press moderately until the oil is distilled or rises from the ear; and the patient will feel the scent within, and let one spoonful of the distillation be heated with fire as if it were being distilled in the ear; and ensure that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be very good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the earstopping
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without having at least one hole in the ear; and this same thing happens with adults due to an ear infection or puss within the ear, and this ear infection sometimes completely fills the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small amount of pus discharged from the ear, which can be clearly seen.
