Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it comes in completely and cannot be seen, it is of grave healing in various positions, and in such a case, you must place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, you should open it entirely with that spatula as shown here:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And should be entirely sharp in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the opening is of flesh or cartilage of the ear, you should hold with subtle tweezers, and strike gently until the cartilage is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the opening is deep in the ear, take a sharp, subtle probe and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the ear canal. If you feel the opening causing pain to the patient when they hear, pierce gently, but do not harm the nerves of the ear; then insert an ear wick according to the size of the wound, and moisten with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Apply this daily until the wound is healed, take a linen cloth and soak it in rose oil and powdered vitriol; if you see the ear swelling, then pull out the first cloth and apply another linen cloth soaked in ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling disappears; then heal it until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If there is a flow of pus, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments to remove the flow of pus which are either distillation methods.
de la char des papieres	of the wood from paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is a remedy that comes on paper for the eyes when they are moist and dry; you must stretch them with tweezers and scissors, and then press them with a spatula from their roots; then put vitriol powder on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not work, you should cauterize it with the subtle cautery of the lens and then cauterize after incision; many times they heal, but nothing stays from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times in paper, there come things that appear like hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason, the disease is called "hail", and it consists of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: keep watch to see if the hail becomes quiet from both sides, and it is a light thing to know; then make an incision on it, next, peel off each part gently, then take the forceps and crush it. If you cannot cover it without puncturing the paper slightly, do not worry the patient at all; if the tear is large, gather it together with stitches, and cure it until it heals; if it is small, do not apply force, for oil will restore it soon enough.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and grab the hail with forceps, crush and press it from both sides; if the paper is moved by the incision, do not worry; when the hail is crushed, apply salted oil and cure the wound of the one who has swelling until the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is infused into cloth made of paper above, and it happens more in children than in adults, and it greatly affects their eyes, and they come down with catarrh at mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hurry to their eyes; therefore, they lie on their faces immediately, sleep above them, and their papers are damp under their eyelids that the exinach spreads and covers its appearance in oil. And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places his head in your hand; and then take one cloth made of linen, and arrange a tent-like circle according to the amount of exinach from each part, then put it over [the eye]; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is collected within the circle; then make a small incision in the moist area with a sharp spatula, but not larger than the wound you would make when opening a vein; and cut the skin completely until you see the exinach; and in multiple positions, the exinach comes from the incision, according to the form of a white piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then hold the cloth tightly between your hands and turn your hand to both sides until it is spread out; and ensure that you do not damage the incision, that you do not reach the oil with the spatula, or that you do not cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not open at the start of the cut, raise a little the incision lightly until it appears; then pull it out as we have said, then moisten cloths in oil and water, and place them on top, and hold with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who grind seeds and place them on top to destroy the moisture that remains. Then heal it until it is healed. If an abscess becomes hot at the location, cure it with plasters cooling it down until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hair of the papyrus (meaning: plants or fibers resembling hair)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper lice are born with hair other than nature's, and they are raised, they harm the eyes, and bring on kinds of diseases such as habitual weeping and swelling of the paper lice and albugine, all due to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to cure them: either by cauterization with fire, or by medicinal heat as mentioned in the previous chapter on cauterization, or by incision and stitching, or by caustic substances, as I shall explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper lice from the oil onto your left hand; if it changes color, that is good; if not, push a needle through one filament of it; and remove the margin of the paper or where the hairs grow from those hairs, taking one filament across the whole paper, and shave it; then make an incision in the part beneath the paper, under the hairs adjacent, covering the whole spatula, from the large tear to the small one; then pull one filament, and place a small tent of cloth and linen under the paper, then mark on the paper a hook-like figure, like a mirte berry, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity with which you intend to lift the paper as previously designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	If you need to cut a large quantity of the paper according to how much the paper is softened; then make an incision across all the lines you have marked, starting from the large tear to the small one; and it should be one of the slits near the natural hairs at the root of a radish, then insert the onion in one of the two angles of the cut, then peel it entirely; then close the two lips together with a stitch using one thread of fine linen, and squeeze out the blood, and make adhesive the excess filaments on the scissors with any sticky substance, if you choose to do so; if not, do not bother with it, then leave the stitch and the threads for 2-4 days; then treat the wound without stitching with drying and constricting substances, because the paper heals at the edges of the wound and by its assembly, but the stitch is soaked (as the ancients say), and it is work done without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another manner: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure similar to the fennel stalk, as we have mentioned, divided into three sections according to the following form:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which stands above the small sections equally according to the following form:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the ability to hold the pliers and the figure is not equal, take a needle with one thread, and put it into the figure; and place another thread through the large hole, and another through the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your hands; then raise your hand equally, and remove all the skin on which you have marked, as we have mentioned, then sew together the two lips of the wound with stitching, and heal it until it is healthy; if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar calming ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the hair of the paper turns: you should use what we have said about incision; but stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of canines is as follows: you should fold the paper and place it inside as I have said, and then make two canines by hand, and two thin stitches equally long as the paper and the width of the spatula; take the two heads of the two parts where you hold the threads; then carefully assemble the one above the other on top of the paper covered with oil, and bind the two canines of the two parts together; leave it for some days, and the skin that is tightened will rot and die, leaving a hole through which pus can escape.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long or if you need to force it, then cure it until it heals; when the wound is closed and the paper can be removed and no longer pricks the hairs; this is the shape of the two canines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The tasks are such that you take a fine needle, and tie a thin silk thread to it; then assemble the bones carefully and join them delicately, and make sure the lengths of the threads form a palm's length; then prepare another thin silk thread briefly, tie its ends together; then place the patient's head in your hand; expose the work area to sunlight so that the task is clear, for it is a subtle and delicate procedure; then push the needle into the hole where the hair is alongside, and make it pierce through the skin hastily but not through the natural skin; then pull out the hair up to the assembly, and push the pulled-out hair into the assembly, if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand until the hairs come out entirely with the natural skin.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the bones are treated and the hairs do not come out with them, you will pull out the bone with the thread that you have prepared, until the bone emerges from the wound and can be seen through the oil; then pull out both the bone and the thread, close the wound and leave it for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh heals; if the hairs are small, take a long hair from the head naturally and let it grow with that one, until it is elongated and then cut it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purulence of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or porriture comes in the oil, it occurs in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It happens suddenly through a wound, cut, or cauterization, or similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	The method of work is that you cut the suture, separate the lips of it, and put inside linen bandages, and let it stay until it heals; and it should not be used in its treatment with things that dry up and constrict. For if you do this, the disease worsens more than before; but work with things softening, such as fenugreek; and a poultice of warm or hot water and flaxseed oil should be prepared, and immediately apply it to one side, and treat it in this way.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the secret of your cure is that you must not suture it in its previous form; and this work that we have mentioned is not far from correcting this disease, so that it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh that comes into the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wounds and tears and cauterizations and similar things; and the process of work in it is that you take a needle, in which there are two threads, and pierce the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear to the right one, so that the threads come out in two heads of the flesh; then put the flesh on top of the whole needle, and cut with a spatula as wide as a thumb.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is required, it is good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or cuts within the paper; and may the heads of the two incisions be at the four angles of the incision that you made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter which has the name "J Grecque"; then remove that flesh, according to the thickness that its sides are pointed below it, next to the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then cure it with the medicines mentioned above for softening, and ointments, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the sickness comes from a cut or stitch or cautery, then you must make a clean incision under the hair on the paper, as described above; then squeeze between the two leaves of a glove, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the illness, for it is very diverse in form; and wise masters prepare all kinds of devices with every possible means to make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what work and instruments are needed in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	under the skin of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this type of suture occurs in a man's hand in such a manner that the paper above is sewn with white oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must press the tip of a razor blade beneath the paper and lift it up; hold it with pliers until you extract the substance from the spatumile (a thin, delicate instrument), which should not be too sharp or too jagged, so that the patient does not suffer from the overly sharp spatumile that might hurt the oil; and make your incision, from which you remove the assembled tissue, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural form. The entire assembly is then healed, and sometimes in the oil it becomes infected, with acid and pus; then place a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put wool moistened abundantly with egg on top of the oil. After three days use colloids and healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail has two kinds: one is nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, and another that is not nerve-like but resembles white congealed moisture; when it is touched by iron and cooked with tweezers, it cannot move; and both look like they are beginning towards the great lachrymal, and grow little by little until it covers the entire eye and all the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take a piece of paper in your hand, then pick up the nail with tweezers of small double curvature, and place it above; then take a needle, and put one horse hair or cow hair and strong thread; bend the point of the needle a little and pierce it into the nail, and pierce through the entire needle, and tie the nail with thread and place it above, and scrape all the hair from the side of the nail that follows the lid and the sinew to the hair until the root of the lachrymal, then scrape the remainder in the root of the lachrymal with a subtle spatula and small forceps, leaving the natural tear duct or lachrymal intact; and sometimes the nail is placed on the eyelid only, and at the end, as we have said; then scrape off all the spatumile from which this shape is formed:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep the spatula not to touch the skin tissue and break it, and that the pruning iron is not pierced; and after the incision pour oil a little bit of crushed egg yolk, and from collyrium made of litargyre, and leave it until the next day; then treat it with what is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerve-filled, and you cannot push a needle, and the unguis can't enter, many times this appearance of nail is treated with medicine; and they grow as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, open the oil of the patient, and take the spatula lightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail gently, and if you see that it does not thin out at all and the reason is pressing on it, distill from your mouth into the oil of collyrium made of litargyre and red collyrium and crushed egg yolk, and stop the oil until the next day; then repeat the other work according to this same process, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the oil, like an abscess heals, then milk it, and first heal the abscess hot until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the wound deteriorates in oil due to great harm, then suspend it at the onion, and cut a part of it but not all, so that tears do not come; then distill red collyrium oil made of litargyre.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The first hairs of some men sometimes grow red and cover the eyelid, sticking to the paper and turning towards the outside like a rosebud on a balsam plant; and this condition is such that the patient places their head on your hand, then you open the eyes, and if all the hair is suitable for it, hold it with force; then cut the first red growth, and continue cutting until smooth to the end, taking care not to injure the eye during the procedure; and make the incision with a spatula as described in the treatment of the nail and the small forces used to remove the scrotum, according to the form demonstrated after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the hair is removed, apply oil of linseed or you break and distill red oil, or medicines corrosive, and place the oil outside, with egg white soaked cotton to ensure that it stays hot; and if anything remains, and the wound becomes cold, and you doubt it's hot, leave the oil and cure the wound with cooling agents for reducing heat; then return to your work when the wound is healed, and do this for each hair treated in this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you dilute the treatment of each oil with natural oil and an accidental way with iron work, and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is strong enough to bear this procedure.
des voines des eulz	The veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	These are the red veins that are covered over the oil and carry out their work and weaken the oil all day long. Therefore, it is necessary for you to first examine if the oil, in which these veins are, is normal, and if there is no other disease but the oil; then proceed in this manner: instruct the patient to place his head on your hand, then gently press those veins throughout their entire length according to your wisdom, and let the pressure be subtle double, as follows:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two degrees of pressure in one stroke according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gather the veins delicately and squeeze out the blood hour after hour until you see them move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatula, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that you don't cool the veins; and when you have done this, if it distills green and red oil, it will correct those who are clotted.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you cannot collect all of it in that hour, make a poultice with soothing things on the oil to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is relieved and the abscess is certain to heal, then continue according to this method as before until it heals; and this is the form of cauterization:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil duct
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not cured, there is a defect in it that you should incise above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then repair it with all the instruments mentioned here; it is called "rough head", and it should be made like a new head, pointed like a limestone as shown in the following figure:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the corrupt bone on its base, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is crushed; do this once, then restore the location of medicinal extracts.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is welded together and pus forms, if the body of the bone is welded together and remains thus for 40 days without healing or becoming abscessed, and no bad accident occurs (knowing that it is healthy); but if not, there is no other remedy than to return the fistula to the pit of the newborn according to this form: and you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with medicines hot, and when it is uncovered, take .1 foret according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and the shaft be attenuated up to the tip as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put it on the bone of the elbow and move your hand away from the oil by one inch, then turn the iron completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the veins if he holds his hand above his newborn; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the pus dries and hardens the joint, the matter goes to the newborn; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the flow of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are widely open and do not close of their own accord, you should hold the patient down; then clean them, apply mustard or honey without piercing, then put oil (made of acacia and aloe, incense, and sarcolocola) on it, and hold the oil in place with bandages and cloths. The type of cloth to use is such that you take soft cloth, fold each one into four, and place one on top of the other according to the amount required by the eyes; then hold them together with a firm bandage, and continue applying mustard or honey without piercing; then remove the mustard or honey and leave the oil in place for a day and night; if the oil becomes soft, you should tighten it more; then remove the oil after a day and night, and if you see the eyes healing, that's good; if not, continue applying the oil and cloths and the bandage until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The open wound of the eye does not heal on its own.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the cloudy eye, it becomes like grains of resin and is visible to see; then if you see it covered, the remedy is as follows: take an awl and insert it into the root of the affected part up until where you want it to stop, then insert another awl or thread doubled at the tear duct; and make it pierce, leaving the first awl in place according to its position; then tie a piece of thread around the eye socket and tighten it, then remove the awl and put oil-soaked linen on it; leave it until the filaments grow with the eye, cure the oil with soothing things until the wound heals; sometimes the wound is held in place by the eye itself with a circular piece of cloth around it until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear swollen, pierce them with a thin spatula coming from pure oil, clear the pus, and close it up immediately; then draw it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	with a thin spatula coming from pure oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This illness called "alcunnati" is not far from a bowel that has been assembled in oil, appearing like an ulcer draining pus, but it is not an ulcer; and the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit on a chair with his legs apart and feet flat on the ground. Then take the head between your two hands, move it as much as you see the bowel come towards the eyes; then insert it, and do not drain nor expose the light, let the patient see things as he is accustomed to; and if the draining of the bowel does not appear, know that it is an ulcer, and if the draining of the bowel has not been prepared as we have said. place the patient between your hands, then take a thin spatula and press it on the cornea-covered cloth .i. inch along the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal cloth and the cornea, until the bowel emerges; and when it has emerged, let it distill into hot boiling oil mixed with honey or fenugreek oil and honey, then let it be cured with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	The sharp points of oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the resemblance of sharp points in the division and what is necessary for piercing; if it works according to health. You must make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from light due to the sun, and hold the oil tight and very firmly; then place the paper of the oil on your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or on your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand (if the eyes are left-handed), the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand (if the eyes are right-handed); then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the thickness of a reed in that hollow of the oil at the lesser angle, then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and hold your hand as long as it pierces through the hollow of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty place; and the measure of the way almagda should be to the full of the measure of the space which is from the prunelle to the end of the black part; this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the waxed paper, then put the instrument up to it or where the sharp point is, then press down along another path. If the sharp point now comes out, the patient can see it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest and if the sharp point retreats along the second path, put the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not move, gently turn almagda around your hand bit by bit; then replace in trepanation a small amount of gemstone oil, and let it flow inside. Then place a stopper made of oil-soaked cloth or moistened linen on the trepanation hole, and seal it with holy oil. We and those of our time put on top a mixture with much egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the oil due to its hardness, since there are some men who have excessively hard hairs, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which is shaped like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Then perforate only the conjunctive and do not go too deep, but make it thin; then insert almagda as previously mentioned; and to complete the work, prepare a sleeper for the patient, in which he lies on his back in two layers; and be attentive to all movements; take light foods; and move neither head nor neck, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see certain things, and then rebind him for seven days; and it is not advisable that you do this during the treatment or after the incision immediately, but it is advisable to alleviate it because the pain rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess comes up, you should unbind the oil before the seventh day, and direct one who knows how to assuage abscesses; and when it is pacified, then unbind the eyes and place a small eye cup over them for any duration, and remain in that dark room. And gradually leave the house bit by bit, and convert yourself to your home; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in his country, people do almagda piercing, which causes the water to come out, but I never saw anyone with it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the ancient books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they should be specifically:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And these are the characteristics of the heads of this same subtlety, and the rear parts in four corners sharp.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At no time do various strange sores born on the neck arise, of which there are some that seem like scorpions with many prongs; and if such a sore is swollen in this way or it has a sore swollen in another color, and if the sore is soft of bone color. In the case of those sores that are soft but not swollen, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, pour vinegar on these sores, and pull them out; then hold what you can with a thin sharp spatula until you know that this sore is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be held, you must cut it all off with delicate instruments gently, so that nothing remains; and if without being cauterized or bandaged, the abscess bursts, the remedy is as necessary; and if these are malicious abscesses, you should hurry and burn them with cautery until the pus is drained and all the sores are removed, then pour oil of roses or vinegar on the wound.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. If the patient does not work, moisture approaches up to the palace (palace = head), and you should know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pierce as required, you should know that there is pus in the bone above, so the instrument does not come for cutting: then you must put a string of flax (flax = lin) about half an inch thick and white into his nose, with a space of less than one finger between each knot; and insert the patient's head through the string in its nostril to the deepest part of his mouth; and do this several times as children in school often do, and it is easy for whoever wants to do it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and be familiar with one after another while we are who are holding the string. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted the pus, then pull out the flax, squeeze the blood, and moisten the flax in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything remaining of the pus; and then put a reed (reed = plonc) in his nose for some days until he is healthy, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as it is called when oil and medicines are distilled in the head.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or brass, resembling a lamp with an open neck, like a cane, and lead it in the same way; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the pus in the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times, a disease called "telul" arises in the head of the neck and grows larger and larger until it can be seen with the eye; therefore, you should cut it at the beginning, and boil it completely, then put the cautery or burning medicine on it; and if it is delayed to be cut when it is large, take care if it is hard, of a reddish color, and has poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an enlarged abscess, for when it is cut once, much harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft-touched and not of reddish color, you can cover it completely; empty the patient and cut cautiously, cure the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilage joints, it benefits little, except in some men. Therefore, if this happens to anyone, you should check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together in a stitch, heal it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from both sides, you must cut all the skin on their edges as much as they bleed, then join the two lips together in a stitch, tighten, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood sandalwood, and incense crushed; and put some plaster of strong or other plaster over it, and let it remain until it dries up, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the stitching is such that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the abdomen stitching; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	about abscesses from lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Within the lips there often arise hard abscesses, resembling grains of wheat, both small and large; then you must turn the lips, and cut above each tooth, and take it with forceps and crush it in each part; then apply the lee of vitriol ground, until the wound is cauterized; and then anoint the wound with oil of asafetida, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the jaws
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often a swelling arises on the jaws, which the ancients called "albulus"; you must hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, leaving the wound open; then apply vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders to it; if the swelling returns after incision, which often happens, cauterize it again; it will not return after cauterization; and these are the shapes of the instruments for cauterizing.
des sordens	Of the sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are ulcers in the roots of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and harsh; sometimes the teeth become black and yellowish and decaying, when corruption comes to the gum, and they stink; you must have the patient sit on your lap, with his head in your hands, and remove the sores or the decayed teeth as far as possible; then clean the blackness and greenness, and the yellowish and other impurities until they are purified; if you remove that which is at the root, it is good; if not, start again on the second or third day, until everything is cleaned; know that teeth have different shapes of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work shows, because the person who cleans the teeth has other shapes than the one who cleans between the teeth; and these shapes and others are provided with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay the drawing for as long as possible, for this should not be done at all; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to shave it off.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Adonques quant li malades est contraints du tirer, il faut que tu sois certains de la dente douillante. Maintes fois desoit le dolor le malade, et croit qu'elle soit ou dente sainte, et fait tirer la bonne dent; mais toutefois ne se départit pas le dolor par ceux, tant que le mauvais reste, car nous l'avons déjà vu faire à ces saints; et quand tu es bien certains de la dente douillante, il faut que tu escorches entour la dent à tout endroit. Mespule fort pour protéger la gencive de toutes parties; puis le mouvez à tes doigts ou aux tenailles subtiles au premier coup et coup par coup, tant qu'il soit bien éclochiés, puis y afferme bien les tenailles; et soit les chefs du malade dans ton saint entre tes genoux, et le tien bien si que il ne se mouve.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling the tooth out straight to break it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and push it gently from each side, and move it as you have done before. And if the tooth is pierced and chewed, it is necessary to fill it with bandages where the holes are; and hold it subtly with tweezers so that it does not break while being pulled out; and it must be worked very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not break it [the dislocated joint], and leave a part remaining, and return pain to the patient by the malice of the root, causing them greater pains than the first. And beware that you do not act as ignorant lords who, through their haste and bravery, sometimes break the chariot [bone] and do not bring about what we have stated; but they often cause this great disease due to the roots that remain, or because of the chariot that they break, as we have often seen; and when the teeth are separated, wash the area with wine or vinegar and oil; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if it does not work, cauterize [the wound].
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the forceps, which first silence the teeth, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you separate the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should be large enough so that they do not bend when separating, and should be made of good iron, and serrated for holding onto the teeth.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	If the root remains exposed when pulling, you must put moistened soft cotton on it for 1 day or 2 until the gum is softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri," so that the teeth seem like a beak of a plier; and inside them should be made as if a chisel and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, you must uncover the entire cheek around the root and use the instrument called "althali," which is known as plier, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be large and thick so as not to break, and if the root jumps out through them, that is good; if it does not, help with all tools, from which the shapes come later.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And help with this tool having two prongs, of which this shape comes from it:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other iron objects that are in front of the teeth roots, and with this tool resembling large pliers, from which this shape comes:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument must not be able to break, and know that many dense instruments are; and likewise other instruments, which are not counted; and wise masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the sickness require, for there are various diseases in which the ancients did not teach an instrument; and if it breaks the chariot or other bones, which it should not, then seek the instruments that are required, as I have said, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and firm to hold the bone so that it does not slip away but can be held and removed; and then restore the joint with appropriate medicines, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, use the entire instrument for that purpose:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to natural shape and are misshapen, especially in young women, you must know if the root is not near the tooth, and it is not in its proper position, and it cannot be straightened or filed. In that case, extract the tooth; and if it is erupted with the tooth, take the instrument as shown in the figure below, which resembles a small beak, and is made of sharp iron at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth, little by little in many days, due to hardness of the dentin, and because you cannot move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, file it with a small steel file as shown below in form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is similar to the file used for making needles; and with the file, file the tooth little by little in many days lightly, so that it does not move until it becomes smooth; then flatten it at the end with any smoother, and if the dent is too sharp and it bites the tongue, you must file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth are dislocated, either by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot chew due to pain and they vomit, you treat them with constricting medicines but it is not effective; then they must be restrained with a gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never does; and let the thread be medium size neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you observe the teeth, take the thread and put it between two healthy teeth on both sides, as many as there are, one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering up to the part where you started, and hold your hand skillfully and carefully, so that it does not move; and let your knot be at the tooth root so that it cannot escape. Then tie the teeth with the thread using pliers, and assemble them, and place them back between the healthy tooth, and make sure it does not injure the tongue; then leave it tightened as much as it can stay, and if it dislocates or the threads break, tighten another one; if it remains and serves for a long time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the guidance of the two healthy and two misaligned teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.
