And when the teeth fall out and are put back in place repeatedly as we have said, let no one intervene who is not skilled and patient; and sometimes they make the shape of a tooth of cattle bone, and place it at the location where it is missing, and tie it in place as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	1. Sometimes this ligament comes below the tongue naturally, and it is born in such a way; or due to accidental wound healing; and the treatment is as follows: you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head still, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is suddenly of a wound, you press the uncine and cut wide the ligamented part; and make sure that the incision is not too deep, because an artery is underneath; and when you have done, lift up the swollen and inflamed area with warm rose water and salt water, or cold water, then put a flax tent under the tongue; and tie the patient's tongue each night so the swelling cannot spread. And if discharge of blood comes, you put vitriol powder on it; and if the wound does not heal, you cauterize it with the slow cautery, which is good for this. Then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a small, black or hard color that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, pour vitriol powder on it until it burns, then return to your work until you drain everything; then lift up the swollen and inflamed area with warm salt water, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	At times, boils called "godath" come inside the throat. These are properly called the two almonds. When you treat them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard, small abscess of dark color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of blood flow; but let it be until it becomes ripe, and then you will cut it, or it would burst by itself; and if it is white in color, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument for covering, but first check whether the abscess's heat has subsided and been calmed. Then make the patient sit in the sun, and his head should be in your hand, and open his mouth and take the sergeant between his hands, and press the tongue underneath the entire instrument, which is its shape; it can be made of silver or fine brass as well as a small knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue with the entire instrument and see the abscess. Take the awl and pierce it into the almond, pulling it out farther than you can; take nothing from the cloths with you, then cover it with the instrument, which resembles a cork; even if the head is bent, one end to another, and are very sharp, made of iron or copper:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the base with pliers, here is its shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the base with pliers, here is its shape: (continued)
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside the throat, to be precise, one small abscess; and I had her throat tightly closed, so the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passageway, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died within a day or two. The abscesses were swollen so much that they filled two fingers through the nostrils. So, I pierced one of them immediately, pulled it out, and removed a large piece of pus; then I closed the other nostril, opened her mouth, and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses, cut a part of them, and did not let any pus out except a small amount; and thus the passageway in the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water first and then wine, and she continued to cut the abscess for a long time; the abscesses kept growing back, filling up the space I had vacated, until it became very large; at that point, I tricked it by inserting probes deeper into her throat and cauterized it within her throat. In this way, the abscess stopped growing, and I left those parts alone, and God did with them what He wished after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye swells and elongates, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are eased, and it is thin, you must cut it; and the one that is rounded and assembled but not long; and it is blood-colored or of dark color or black, you must make an incision in it. For there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it as I have said, according to its thickness and length, you must make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier; then insert the probe into the eye, pull it out, and cut it at .i. of 2 punctures that I have said in the incision of 2 almonds. And you must not cut more than the superfluity beyond the natural limit; for if you do so, it hurts the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we have said in the incision of 2 almonds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of being cut, you must use an instrument for cauterization to reduce fear. And the method of cauterization is hot. And it is that the patient places his head on your lap, and then presses his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and touch it with hot coals, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a lock of hair or ointment container that the medicament is put into, like a spoonful of cuillier, and place the instrument full of medicine onto the eye; and the patient lies on his side so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine inside, not to the throat and the nose; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it onto the eye until you see that it is swollen and the irritation caused by the medicine has subsided; then take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument filled with cotton into the canal above, until the cotton adheres to the eye; do this repeatedly until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. If you have to start the cauterization again, repeat it, and after the cauterization, clean the area around the eye with a mixture of cotton in butter, and wash what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargarismes until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective through fumigation rather than cauterization; if it is treated by this method, take camomile, yarrow, origanum, rue, and fennel or similar herbs, place them all together in one pot, and add water; boil the mixture; let the pot be well sealed with strong clay; and have one instrument with hairs inside the pot as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be made of silver or copper, and let one of the eyes be pushed into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the cane while the eye is being mortified; after this process continues until the eye dries up, but ensure that you do not begin this procedure at the beginning of an abscess boil, as many things may happen; and never perform this unless in the decline of the abscess boil. And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and place a chicken egg crack inside the patient's head so that the mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and it is good treatment along with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or other sharp object lodges in the throat, so you must draw out what you can see and press the tongue against the instrument until you see movement in the object; if it does not open and remains lodged in the throat, make the patient vomit before the food is fully cooked in the stomach; by chance, the object may be expelled through vomiting. Or, the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or a small piece of dry bread; tie one thread to the sponge and then swallow it; when it reaches the location, it will adhere, and then you draw it out; if it does not come out as mentioned above, take a splint-shaped instrument as follows:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And bend the instrument into a curve towards the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and lift the head high; beware not to touch the epiglottis, let the patient put the instrument in, because he must move or the matter is worsened; if he pushes it down, or draws it out completely, keep the instrument equal until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the saliva is used as medicine, as I have said in the division, for curing medicines; and when it does not help, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, because you press the tongue on the instrument that I told you about. And if you see the saliva, take a small pair of scissors or delicate pliers that are suitable for this purpose. If that is not effective, then take a threaded needle, and put it in the patient's throat, and insert the tip of the needle with hot iron at its end repeatedly. And anoint the patient with cold water throughout the day. Then take a full ounce of cold water, open the mouth, pour it into the mouth without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the saliva feels the cold water, it will spill out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then subdue the patient with astringent [medicine], in the instrument that I have mentioned for the astringent treatment of the eye; do this many times, because it will require more persistence. The manner of the astringent treatment is that you take one pot or one with charcoal, and cover it with a perforated cloth, and place the head of the instrument in it; then pour your astringent, and the patient puts the chief of the cane in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that no smoke escapes, but comes only to the nostrils; and the nose will require persistence, and if it does not fall, continue the astringent treatment many times; allow the patient to suffer thirst, and eat salty and sour things, and drink nothing of water; then it will be necessary for it to come out by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument for treating the nose is such that, when it can be seen, resembles curved tweezers to enter the throat; and it should resemble a syringe nozzle, and have an abrasive tip made of lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many things resembling an abscess are mentioned hereafter in this book according to what memory recalls from one and another, and they are diverse in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that the first resembles [the other], and of these, one is in its similarity and due to moisture. And the second manner is concerning joints situated on the body. For abscesses of the head are different than those from the foundation, and abscesses of the charnut joint are different from those that come at jointures, and each should have its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if it is not necessary to perforate abscesses while the boil has yet matured according to its completion; and for those that must be perforated when they have become hard, and do not die according to their maturity, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when an abscess comes near a joint, and it is left until it bursts, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint become rotten, which causes contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is near the main member, and you delay the perforation until it has matured, it will harm the main member; or if it is near the foundation, if it is perforated before it has matured; it must not be perforated without the abscess having completed its digestion, except for those that are near the foundation, which could not be penetrated and become long inside, and a fistula forms; and it cannot heal in a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for perforating an abscess that has matured according to its completion, and it is when the pain is relieved, and the fever subsides, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and shrinkage of the abscess's head, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where it depends less on the abscess, and where it has opened up; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places or where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those who are swollen, it should be aligned according to the affected limb. And when an abscess is in a charred area, it is better to leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body will flow out of the opening, and it will be full of foul matter; and there may be hardening of the wound edges and its deepening. And for any abscess that are pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limbs require. And you should apply small incisions, small openings; and large abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is necessary to cover with care, and dress; when it has become as thin as cloth, and softened, it is necessary to do as with babies: and for those that are cut into four angles, and for those from which one cuts like the leaves of myrtle, like abscesses in the joints; and for those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar dressings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no head (i.e., if the abscess is superficial), it should be pierced completely; and when the abscess is large, and has accumulated a great amount of pus, you should pierce it, but not draw out all the pus at that time, but only a part of it; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing incorrectly; do this repeatedly, gradually, until the pus is completely drawn out. This applies to patients who are weak, women, children or old people. The body may sometimes jump with the release of the pus, which might cause the death of the patient, and you should be careful about that. Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it should be stuffed in each one with linen or old cotton; and for a large abscess, where there are many cuts, you must pack in cotton or wool of flax without moisture, and bind until the third day; then remove it, and heal with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and wine, and wet a cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly.  And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book should be used on the affected area; and if it is winter, or the wound or abscess is very nervous, then you must apply heated and wet cloths (tents and drapes) to it.  And if it is summer, and the limb is fleshy, then you must apply cold and wet cloths, or cold and frozen cloths, for up to three days as we have said; and then drain the abscess, lance it, and treat it until it heals completely.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And you should know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	1. For small abscesses that come in the head, our methods are as if in cloths, just like a bladder of a grape, and there are many similarities. There are some fat ones with moisture, as well as some hard and stone-like ones without doubt that the arteries do not oppose. And concerning the procedure of the abdomen, you must try it out on every instrument which is called "entromissoire", from which this form follows, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, they cut above the long one. And when the moisture is emptied, they peel off skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again when nothing is left; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is available; otherwise in water and oil, and apply it to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and let it rest overnight. And replace the cotton the second day, as before, on the third day, until you know that it does not remain overnight; then cure the wound with ointment appropriate, until it is healed. And if the abscess contains one notch of fat, cut it along this form, long; and pour your eyes into it, and peel off skin from all sides, and apply your entire care to drain the pus where it lies; and if the arteries oppose you, do as I told you before. And similarly do for a hard or stone-like abscess, and treat and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting on a hard abscess and the moist one is easier, because they contain little blood. And if any of these abscesses or head have no moisture, and from those was the abscess that I cut on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone core, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had pierced it with anything, one would have made as much of a wound as a stone. In other abscesses coming from heads, especially those that come from children's heads and roots of the ears, they should always be opened for as long as possible, because pus comes out; and they should be cured as needed.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Often this abscess appears at the neck, under the ears, and in the groin, and sometimes it appears in other parts of the body, and they are large and swollen. Each scrofula is located within its coat, as the nodes of the neck and head described earlier; and the resemblances of these scrofulas are many. Some contain moisture, and some are malignant and do not want to obey health. In that case, when you see it in good condition for incision, resembling the color of the body, silent on all sides and not pressed against the neck artery or vein, and not deep; then you must cut over it, scrape each part, and place two incisions with the knife, if necessary, as described in abscesses of the head; and draw it out bit by bit, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and the spatula should not be too sharp or cutting, that the hand does not slip, and do not see too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not let you pass over, put vitriol powder in the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are appeased and the wound is softened and begins to rot. And when the blood is stopped, return to your work; then ask your assistant if there remain any small scrofulas, if they cut them and clean them. And if there is a large root of the scrofula in the vein, it is not necessary that you cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang down without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you scrape the entire scrofula (boil), it is necessary that you gather the two lips of the wound and sew them up immediately, for there will be no superfluous delay due to the size of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it (the boil) and draw pus, and sew as we have said. Those scrofulas with superfluidity, pierce where the opening is already wide; and pierce in the same way as the one mentioned earlier, by depending on it, then introduce lancets with ointment and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply an enchanting ointment until it heals.
de squinance	If the scrotum becomes inflamed and swollen, apply a poultice to it made from crushed barley, wine, and oil. Repeat this process daily for three days.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and wrote about the shape of the throat, but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the slit in the throat called "epiglote" be opened; and no aid should be given by these, because all the veins and the parotid gland of the sick are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in 2 mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the parotid gland, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid the strangulation that comes from the swelling.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglotte, it is necessary that we make the incision below four circles or three small incisions through the transverse, between the four circles or by the amount of the incision of the siphac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the joint is difficult to cut through at the incision of the epiglottis, there is no cartilage, and the veins are long in that place.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat all along, then cuts open the windpipe until he reaches the trachea; and avoids the veins of blood, if you see anything, and then severs the thyroid gland as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by cutting open the windpipe that if it jumps out through the broken place, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And let the wound remain open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt of strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound with care, and stitch it up entirely to touch the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing until it becomes healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged dead, and the flight has fled.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then you cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and it is thus preserved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And thus the ancients commanded to leave the wound open as long as the illness is passed, and it is passed in 3 or 4 days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it when it is healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one knife, and she stabbed it in her throat, and cut part of the channel of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was summoned to heal her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood coming out of it, and knew that she had not breathed or spoken except through her throat, and the wind was flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I quickly sewed up the wound, and cured it until it healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And no harm came to the maiden except her voice became red, and she returned afterwards to her position.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in the condition of epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia" and is a large abscess of a bluish color, and it occurs mainly in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is according to two kinds: natural and accidental; where natural has no machine.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is according to two kinds, of which one resembles fatness in us, and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from us through artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it should not be done forcefully except in the small one, and prove and examine it all through the opening.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you prove it like a small swelling and it cannot spread to any vein, then crush it as we crush the nose, and pull off all its skin, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And treat carefully, and heal as necessary, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	from us (we)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways of ours there are, which I will say all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now I must say all the difference between knot and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Dislocation is heat and fever lasting until the boil has passed and the purulence is complete; then the fever rests and the heat subsides.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a knot there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains one sack, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like an abscess, and grows large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are of two kinds, either fatty or moist, and many of them are of such a color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the nose, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments called "entromissoire", according to their shape and the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	The manner of inquiry about abscesses is that you take or the more moist part that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then straighten the joint, and take care not to let it dislocate again.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture corrupts the wound, make it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after straightening the joint there is no moisture, know that it is fat. Then make a cross-shaped incision and take pincers, and gently peel off the skin on both sides, keeping the coat intact so you can pull it out safely.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If you cannot draw it out whole, draw it out piece by piece so that there is nothing left.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if something remains, it will return many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if there is a little left and it does not bother you, fill the wound with some corrosive powder, bind the wound, apply something soothing to the abscess, and treat it with other cures until it heals.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If the wound is large, cut it with two lips and treat it with skin from a pig or other animal.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or otherwise is contrary to you and you hasten and apply the vitriol powder, let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound heals, and allow the boil of blood to subside; then return to cover what remains unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of intersecting instruments, and they are in four kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are four squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses with fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like needles used to sew sacks, and are made of citron cane, or iron, or silver, and the yellow ones have more value, and are more skilled at encircling the boils with fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three types: great, medium, and small, according to the size of the wound's width.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the tumors are similar to each other as you can see here: great, medium, and small; and if there are tumors with two bumps in four ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if there are tumors with four bumps, they are also of four kinds; and if there are tumors with two bumps, there are those with only one bump and they are also of four kinds; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of such creatures is sharp, and those who do not cut it cleanly from one side only are prone to error, because one must scrape the nails there so as not to hit the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these incisions [or wounds], the bandages are applied to the wounds, so that the patient does not injure himself at the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And they have three types: large, small, and medium-sized, as you can see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And one should not use it [the cautery] except in the charnu [charred or burnt] places, such as limbs, arms, breasts, and similar places.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	Occasionally, one makes another small instrument resembling fists of bandages, shaped like this, for draining blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And one applies it [the cautery] sometimes to the place that is healthy to close veins and arteries, and sometimes in this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to corrupt, until they resemble breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain swollen and ugly, and whoever wishes to cure them, it is necessary to be according to this form of the line b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and apply the wound with medicine containing charcoal, then close the two edges of the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast slopes downwards and is deformed due to its size like women, they should be divided into two halves, by two similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	The first part of the line, "de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre," translates to: "so that one is holding the other at the end of one and the other, such that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b to line g."
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then, the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and bring what we have said of stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, as long as it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healthy or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it heal while it consumes the remaining meat and fat, then cure it until it heals.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses in the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses coming from under the buttocks are managed as hard scrofulas where they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those containing moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B to line G:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire hole that is in the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and anoint it afterwards until it heals completely.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula (scrofula is a chronic disease that causes swelling of the lymph nodes), then make an incision as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound opens up, apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The severing of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin that is above it becomes sutured, there are often abscesses, and the same happens at an inflamed vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if it is known in this way because of the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And if you feel it with your fingers, it is felt tightly; and if it is for the vein, then it is round and appears prominent.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is folly to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the eyes and at the angles and near the neck and in other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, the iron cautery treatment should be avoided, and the same applies to those with swelling of the arteries on the head. Make a long incision in their skin above the skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then open the incision with scissors, and carefully separate the artery from the tendons until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert an awl underneath [the dislocated joint], and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie a double thread around the artery for two fingers' breadth, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then insert the space between the two joints with an instrument until the swelling inside it disappears and the abscess is opened;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the remedy with a boil lance until the joint cries out;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this one with ointment following this, as long as it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the opening of the vein, then you should paint your hand with this that you can from the abscess all over the skin;
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then push the needle underneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have it one double thread so that you pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or bind it with one of two parts to each of the two corners with thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread does not pass through, insert another needle under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in four inches;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then compress the abscess until the superfluidity enters it, then compress the superfluidity of the pus and leave that which is connected;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then provide remedies of tentoriums and poultices until it is healed;
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses from nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and vein, they come on nerves when wounded, or from too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the shoulder and wrist, and in all joints where there are joints, and it is a grave abscess, its color resembles that of the body, and it feels pain in many positions.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is pressed hard, the patient feels pain, but it is not fully in the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it must be held completely still from all sides, neither forward nor backward, not above nor below, and the one in the joints should not be covered by iron; for by chance it might contract.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And if it is the head or the forehead, make the skin with a spoon.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and strike at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is large, suspend it by the onion, peel it, then open and sew up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Hanging large lumps
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes there occurs in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease that is called 'fungus' because of its resemblance to toads, and it has thin roots and large heads; and in it there are small and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	I saw one man who had two bellies that were more like toads than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were split open, and ran with moisture constantly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I found and weighed them in one at 16 ounces, and in the other 7 pounds, and their work in incision indicates that you should look to see if the patient is moist; and the color of the arterial blood is white and moist with a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the copah is wide and the fire cautery is present with you, for in cutting there are often too large discharges of blood, and if it flows without your notice, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, take a thread well made, bind the arterial blood as we have said, and leave it for 2 days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then hold it (the affected body part), and do not stop squeezing the thread of plunger until it cuts off the artery, and feels resistance; and if the roots are thick, one may fear to cut through it directly due to the abdomen, but you can certainly cut through half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cauterize it so it does not grow back; then treat the wound and ensure you do not cut the thread that is of a dark color, poor sensation, and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess enlarged, and I will come to treat the scrofula hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the belly is filled [with something]
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the belly comes from a cautery of a wound or a tear in the liver, and it is above the abdomen and contains some of the bulges, as happens in other cases, or blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If it is due to the rupture of the liver and the release from the bowel, its color resembles the color of the body, it is light without pain, and has an opening with various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the rupture of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when you press it with your hands, it returns, and then it comes back, and by chance if it is sutured, it greatly enlarges at the opening of the wound and due to great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is easy, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are filled according to a certain quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to wind-inflammation, it is sensitive to touch, and the operations are that you examine whether its appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or wind-inflammation.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary to let the treatment be. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the belly, you must command the patient to strain their anus, stretch themselves out straight, and then press all around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to press gently between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	Then go around the joint that you have signed with all the splint.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then place half of the abscess above to all the large spoon-shaped scoop.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the nails be tied closed.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open half of the stretched abscess on the thread, and put your thumb in it, and push the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it taken by a splinter, remove it, and push the intestines out through the opening of the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the boil, take hold of it at its base, and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein is obstructed, go around it carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, insert two threads into them, and place the needles around what you have made in a cross shape that you make puncture;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then press the abscess in four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it can be pierced, and cut off the dead flesh by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you strike it when it is soft and pliable, then treat the wound as needed, and cover the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound as needed, and heal the wound.
dou chancre	the boil
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have mentioned in the division the resemblances of chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how to avoid using iron cure; and we say that chancre begins in marriage, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be shaved like a chancre that is on breasts, thighs, or similar places, and must be completely removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, it should not be approached, for I have never seen anyone heal one; no one has ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is to purge the patient once with black bile; then let him purge if there is obvious repletion, then cut the patient into one good length for the operation; then shave your claws or chancre and all the hair from all parts, and remove everything that feels nothing from all parts; let the blood flow freely, and be careful of the wound to your hand or anything, and if the discharge of blood makes you opposed to the incision of an artery or a vein, then cauterize until the blood is coagulated; then heal with another cure until it heals.
de ydropisie	dropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already said in the division the likenesses of edema, and in what way the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only this [edema] should be treated with iron; one must not touch iron in these two likenesses: namely tympanites and yposarche, because it is a deadly thing. When you treat this edema likeness called "edema of the ear" with medicines, and the cure does not help, then observe if the patient is weak or if he has another disease besides edema, such as dropsy of the belly and similar things; do not touch iron, because there is doubt. But if you see the patient strong and without any other disease except edema alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must act thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Place the patient upright on your hands, and have the minister press the belly towards the lower part of the buttocks, then take the pointed spatula according to this form: And it should be sharpened on two sides. But do not make it so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and it cannot bleed.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then observe if the edema is connected to the intestines: in that case, you must make an incision below the buttock 4 fingers right of the anus; and if it is due to liver disease, make the incision on the left side 4 fingers below the navel; and if it is due to the swelling, make it on the right side, and do not allow the patient to lie on the incision so that the excess fluids do not run to the weak place.
