puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the entire hide with the instrument, and push it, and place your hand all around the spatula between the skin and the gristle as when peeling an apple of the appropriate size or within; then pierce the gristle until the spatula comes to the right spot, which is the tip of the bone; then pull it and place the instrument in its form: It resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of iron or light steel, and has a small hole on one side. On one side, there are three holes; on two sides, two; and one on another; and the head is shaped like a feather quill, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes carve pens:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top above is the artery, so that when the instrument comes to the bone, move the instrument now on top of it. Empty then either half or one-third because if you look at more than what is necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he will fall unconscious, or approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to its potency, and according to the conditions of the patient's vitality and his pulse; then pull the instrument and hold the artery, which is now held for the caution that stops the holes in the gristle, as I have spoken about, so you pierce it in this manner; then restart the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering from it, and take out a small amount of artery.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day, and be careful not to overdo bathing until it doesn't persist but only a little water. And if you doubt about the patient, and leave him much water, treat with sepulchral earth or hot sand, and by sweating or bath, and expose to sun, and anoint with vinegar; and treat with medicines that dry until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	For stopping the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never are born children who do not have foreskins in the penis, or whose foreskin is small or not in its place. If it should be necessary that it be pierced immediately with a very thin spatula according to this form: then put a thin piece of cloth over the foreskin, and tie and hold it for 2 to 4 days until he wants to urinate, and then remove the cloth, and make him urinate, and then replace the cloth; and accidentally it should not be necessary because the urine that comes out does not leave the cloth closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	He who has a small perforation is to be treated with the plunger of cloth, as we have said, it will widen. He who does not yet have a perforation in its place are blocked, for no one is born who has the perforation at the tip of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upward; and cannot ejaculate due to the material not being able to reach the marris, and it is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of work is that the patient lies supine on his back, with the tip of the penis and the base as thick as a pen's feather, so that the perforation remains in place as needed; and beware of the flow of blood which comes frequently, and if it happens, stop the bleeding from the injured area, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this albate comes in the penis, and it is an appearance of hideous disease; there are both malicious and non-malicious [forms]. You must take them one by one with subtle care, crush and cleanse all of them, then put cotton wool in Egyptian ointment on top, then cure it with fine ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the albate is malicious, of a putrid color and swollen, you must apply cautery. When you have crushed it, if the albate is within the penis and has both skin and skin outside, you must first remove the albate that is inside; and when it is healed, treat the outside. For if you cure them together, there is no assurance that the parts of the penis will not be perforated, and blackness and corruption come into the penis and elsewhere; in this case, you must clean everything that is black and corrupted, then lie ointment made from pomegranate rind and honey on top, and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	If there is bleeding, apply the lunar cautery as follows: The cauteries should aid in two dispositions simultaneously: namely, the bleeding and corruption; if the parts of the penis are corrupted and shrunken, you must lead or induce urine from the penis and make the patient urinate; when the skin is loosened at the tip of the penis which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or it occurs due to injury or abscess, then you must shave the area with a sharp instrument, until the ligaments are released, and release the parts of the penis from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a serious matter to speak of this, then you must lance it with a single spatula, slightly deeper than half the thickness of the rod and skin; then press gently between two fingers, and put a thin piece of damp, cold linen cloth on it, so that it does not immediately heal.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds in that it does not have a constant healing process; nonetheless, when we perform this work of our own will and specifically on infants, it is necessary for us to make the best and easiest work for their salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and healers performing circumcision around one day, using forceps and a new scalpel; however, it was difficult because there were two layers, and sometimes they would cut the wrong one and leave the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound is covered, and there is double pain, and during the cleaning of the tip of the member, the point is not always certain; and during the cleaning of the nail, by accident the iron slips, spoiling the work, and many times it becomes necessary to clean it without need and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the amputation which is done to all the chains of thread I have found the goodness of experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, cut equally all the time; but that the threads be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not bind the thread only around the rod, but allow him to enjoy in every way that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	then let the child's hand be between your hands straight, and press the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them nor any of the instruments; then push your hand to the rod and blow or cut, and draw it up until the joint of the rod is even; then clean it well from the dirt that has assembled there, then tie the marked point with a double thread, then bind each finger to another thread; and hold it two fingers apart by the second binding and cut the knuckle as close as possible and pull the head of the rod.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the pus flow drop by drop, for it is purifying; sprinkle powder on top and on the powder put a cloth soaked in egg yolk cooked in rose water, mixed with fresh rose oil, and leave it like that until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the strength for the healing is this: the two shoulders should be tender and sharp, and the shoulders equally as large as the hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the healing is when the marrow inside is at the incision; therefore, you must stretch it to your fingernail so that the wound becomes an abscess; and equalize it, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then take pliers and then press.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they surpass three days, and that which is beneath the scrotum swells, leave it until the abscesses have been calmed and the scrotum is lightly opened; cut it as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the scrotum, this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the affected area with healing powder as we have said in treating powders, and if you cut too deeply, it will go beyond its bounds, but it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, or blood congealed, or pus, or frozen urine, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention due to a stone in the bladder or neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient bend over their knees; and they should put their feet on the back, and extend their abdomen from above the lower back, and hold the patient straight as much as possible; then the neck of the bladder is forced to express the stone above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If it does not come as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the equipment called "siringue", of which this is its form: it should be made of subtle silver, light and slender like a bird's feather; and the cannula should be one and a half palms long and delicate at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the method of the discharge of urine is that you take one double thread, tie one end of it to the tip of a piece of linen or cotton, and push the tip of the thread into the syringe; and plug the surplus of the linen and push it up to the tip of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and have the patient sit on one stool, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and warm water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the anus; then insert the syringe forward up to the bladder, and have the patient feel it come to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide leading where it goes is twisted; then the thread is pulled out little by little, and the urine follows the thread, then pull it out forcefully, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and continue the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient feels relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scratches or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is collected there, and you see it distill liquids and medicines, do everything using the instrument called "clepsydra", and its shape is:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the channels lead so that the medicine can reach the penis without addition, if we can draw out moisture, and push when necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see to throw your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the goat in the moisture, and draw it along with what is inside; if you draw out the moisture from the goat, and then push hard on the drawing, it will enter the goat, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient can feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	This is the form of the subtle enema used to cleanse the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	This is the form of the subtle enema used to cleanse the bladder: it is made of silver or copper, and its head is higher; beneath it are one finger or links. Then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture that you see for cleansing the bladder. Tie it between two fingers with strong twine. Heat one piece of that moisture on fire. Place the head of the enema in the penis, then hold your hand under the bladder with all the moisture coming towards it, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly all around; then put a strong thread in the holes, then assemble the circle like one would close a bag, and put within it oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone (arrowhead or projectile)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stones (arrows or projectiles), and their extraction along with medicines; and I have told the difference between an embedded stone in the body, and all its signs, and when to operate on a stone according to its size; and regarding the bladder, and the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder, resembling a jump in its subtlety; it opens the kidneys, and irritates the patient's penis, and it pains him many times, and then swells; and many foundations come from these jumps; and children's healing is light until they are four years old, and it is very painful in old age, and it is a medium-sized illness to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and tilt them upside down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and rises slightly towards the top; then make him sit between your hands arranged below, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely declining downwards; then press and touch it with your hand.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the cavity, hasten now to cut into the stone above it. And if it does not fall by touching all around it, moisten your left index finger with oil, if the patient is a child, or use your thumb, if the patient is an adult; and push it onto its foundation, seek for the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, pull it out by the neck of the bladder; then press down on it, and push it towards where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upward, and to remove the skin that is below the testicles in the area where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it, so it takes this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And it is made between the one that is between the coccyx and the base, not in the middle but at the side of the lower back on the left side; and it should be straight above the bone, and your hands should be adjacent or at the base, and the incision should be wide enough for passage, but narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance the hands pressing on the base (the hands) may jump due to effort; and be aware that there is such a stone or angle; it is necessary to press hard so that the dislocation emerges easily. And if there is such a one who is soft, resembling a plum, round, from which the dislocation emerges lightly.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Therefore where there is an angle and edge, make the incision larger; and if it does not dislocate, you must pull up on the pliers that are shaped like a chisel at the tip to force the stone to move so that it does not escape; or you put under it the small curved instrument called the clavis; and if you cannot manipulate it in this way, widen one hole with a drill and then remove the bone without cutting it.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one arrow, push the largest one first into the bladder, then strike it, draw it out, and pull out the smaller ones afterwards. If it is very large, it must be cut open to make a larger wound. For the patient, two things happen: either he dies, or urine comes out immediately because the wounds cannot close; but still try to extract or break apart with pliers as much as possible while you pull it apart in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, tightening it, and place one damp cloth soaked in oil and wine or in oil and cold rose water on top, to cool down the abscess; then raise the patient's head and do not loosen the rope until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen the rope, wash the wound well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of diaphinecon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if abscesses boils come in the wound and corrosions, and if blood clots in the bladder, and urine is retained because of this, which is known in such a way that without jumping with urine: therefore, press your hand in the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will rot and burst.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Lift the wound from pus and inflammation and cleanliness, and assist in every way that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the wounds that you treat, that you bind them with two bandages, and gather the medicines on top of the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is guided by the penis and pierced through, and urine cannot come out; you should treat it as I have said earlier, that you cut many times, and there is an excuse for cutting because of this cure. I have already proved it in such a way.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod of this shape and sharpened at four angles on one tip:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then insert the iron rod through the urinary channel under the stone so that it cannot return into the bladder; then gently push the rod into the stone; and turn the rod in the stone little by little until you can pierce the stone from another side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on the part of the stone that is inside the canal. Soon it will be broken, and it will jump out with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then insert one cord under the stone and another above, then make the canal towards the stone between the two ligaments, then pull it out, and cut the ligament, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	From a woman's stone (or pelvis)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rarely that a stone (or pelvis) becomes pregnant in women, and if it ever happens, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that it cannot be found a woman well-informed who exposes herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deeply placed than the stone of the man, therefore it requires a deeper incision, and great fear it causes.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need this, it is necessary that you take a skilled midwife, and if you cannot find one, do not hesitate in any case to take a gentlewoman experienced in the art of women; and present to her a wise woman alive or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and carefully check if the woman is a virgin; then you must insert your finger or base and seek the stone; and if you find it, hold it under your finger, and recommend that she push with her hand or on the patient, and squeeze and press her left hand onto the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If you find it, she must move it little by little from the bladder opening towards the root of the thigh until it reaches the root; then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh in the area where it is moved, and feel the stone in that part; do not move your finger above or below the stone, and cut it off at the first small piece.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then insert the hand into the lower abdomen, if you feel the stone, press the wound so that the stone can come out; and know that there are many types of stones: small or large, sharp or smooth, long or round, and with grooves. Know their appearances to determine the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the bone protrudes, set it in place with powdered vitriol and hold for an hour until the bone is cauterized; then return to your work, until the pain subsides, and have tools that I told you about in the extraction of the stone for assistance in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If the bone protrudes, and it is an artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and hold with tourniquets and bandages, and do not continue to press it, and leave the stone alone and do not draw it, for there is a chance that the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has been relieved and the wounds have healed, then return to your work until the pain subsides.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A watery hernia is nothing but a collection of moisture or white matter, which is under the skin near the testicles, containing an egg; and it is called "white matter", and sometimes it properly belongs within the lining of the eggshell, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the leather of the scrotum between the white matter we have mentioned; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the cause of this watery hernia is weakness that comes to the testicles, and the matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes there comes a blow to the temples, and this moisture can have many colors: either it turns pale yellow, or without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white like we have said, it is an abscess, that is, long like an egg, and does not open the temples, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	and if there is moisture in the very cloth (tissue), it is an abscess with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the hide of the kidneys and the white meat, one feels it well; therefore, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, probe it thoroughly with a probe, so that its shape becomes clear as mentioned before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge what is inside based on the probe that follows.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we treat with iron, it is necessary that the patient be purged to our ability and the fullness of his body; then lie him down on his back, on something slightly elevated, and place many blankets under him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then it is on its left side, instruct the minister to be on its right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the shoulder;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the spatula, strike the cartilage of the shoulder along its length until it is separated from the tip, and let your incision be straight in cutting the cartilage as far as the white part, and remove the cartilage carefully according to your power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the cartilage straight through with one large hole and drain all the water. Then place your fingers, and lift the cartilage upwards. Do not touch the shoulder, but only the cartilage. Strike the rib of it carefully, if you do not strike it skillfully, the water will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the egg (or yolk) jumps out of your work, reset it to its place when you have completed the operation with the syringe; then sew together the two sides of the joint with a suture, then heal it as with other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if the egg (or yolk) is corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you bind the vessels which are suspended, taking care of the outflow of blood; then cut the joint to its entire length, extract the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if an ulcer is assembled in two parts together, know that they are branches; then cut the other part equally as you did the first, draw out the blood, and put dampened flax soaked in rose oil into the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put other damp wool soaked in wine and oil on it, and put two pieces [of cloth] on top, and cover with double layers of fabric, and tie all around with the string as shown in this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two pieces of fabric, make them into bands of damp woolen cloth according to this shape and assemble them on the thigh area, with one piece covering from the base to the back, and the other at the shaft area; and the two ends should be gathered in the belt loop of the braces.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this ramie is used as a fire cautery, the size of an iron blade, and you should take one thin cauterizing knife, cut through the skin at the joints, and heat it as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the fluid is exposed.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If one takes the fire cautery in this manner, and pierces it through to the bone, and burns it with this subtle cauterizing iron:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And hold it in all ways that you can, as long as it is heated up completely; and make sure the fire does not touch the egg (yolk); and know that this work is more effective; and be careful of bleeding, and make sure the incisions are made in order.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if anything happens against it (the cautery), or an abscess bursts or bleeding occurs or something else, then treat what has happened against it as was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is afraid and does not want to wait for this work due to its horribleness, you bring about perforation as I tell you; and it is when you are completely sure by the signs we have mentioned that you pierce the place where the water [collected] is located.
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part, as wide as the spatula, and make the perforation long along the body; and let the wounds be wide, so that all the pus flows out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let the rest of the pus flow out, then treat it until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the white cloth does not allow the fluid to flow from the wound's mouth, you must insert a reed or instrument used to treat fluid from abscesses, as described earlier; then enlarge one finger width the wound, ensure that the fluid returns, and it will heal within 5 to 7 months. Once healed, the patient will recover his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess in the thighs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Ensure that in the section of this rule, there is fear in various situations, so it seems that one should leave it [the abscess];
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you the work and resemblance of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Then many abscesses come from bodies, and especially from the kidneys; and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is known to be due to an excess of sour and acid fluid, which spreads to the kidneys, or by impact;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	The color of an abscess corresponds to the color of the body; it does not feel pain, but is a severe abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance, there is an abscess hard and rough, of such color, and sometimes comes from an artery, or the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, it can be known by the location of the abscess hot, when you press it with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	A person afflicted with swelling of the vein is known by his disposition to the manifestation of the touch of fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can easily perform the incision on this resemblance, and on other sores.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And it is that you cut the core of the boil, then the egg is raised high, and the white streak flows out from the bottom of the boil, and deliver the suspensorium of all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already soft with these newborn sores, then it is necessary to draw out the egg, and cut.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it [the dislocation] is in the breast or within the chest, you must deliver all that cavity and crush it firmly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the navel is located behind the back, you must crush everything and extract the afterbirth as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with damp linen in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess in the cheeks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	this is an abscess covered by a swelling resembling a boil, with the softening of cheeks,
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and when the patient goes, they go quietly.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment of this disease is equally dangerous as described earlier.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and nevertheless we shall tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	You must make the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the suspension device for the eyes below his feet.   (The suspension device is probably for keeping the eyes open during treatment.)
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	stretch out all the vessels that are close to the vein and bind them with the master's thread,   (The "master's thread" is probably the surgeon's or doctor's string used to tie off blood vessels during surgery.)
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	Then apply a sharp spatula wide through the hole where the vessels are exposed, until they are exposed.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then scrape from each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in the temple;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert an awl with one double thread and tie it to the first place where the blood has come out, and tie it again at the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then press the knee straight, in accordance with the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then dress the wound as one would an arrow-shot, so that no pus leaks from either side.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because in this way there is no ill coming, and if all the pus comes out from one side, you must draw out both sides.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of pus, and dry up and cannot heal themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	of the breaking of the nose
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	the consequences of this incision are caused by the opening or breaking of the nose, or the extension on the belly in the area of the inguinal region, due to which the intestines descend from that rupture into one of the openings.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either due to breaking or extension, and these two methods of causing pain come from different sources: either from impact, jump, fall, or lifting a heavy object with a wrong posture, and similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs that this is due to extension of the nose are that it happens gradually, over a long time, and not suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscesses are equal towards the full, because the pus follows the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the surgical incision, which makes sudden pain appear at the beginning, and the abscesses are various appearing under the skin close to it, and this is due to the release of the intestines and the body's reaction to the surgery.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	Sometimes the intestines come out of the circle and are retained, causing great pain to suffer by the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, there is fear, therefore it is advisable to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of work is that you instruct the patient to pull the intestines with their hand inside in the wound, if they can reach it.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then place him on his neck, between your hands, and lift his legs.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the belly upward, and strike the whole hide of the flanks with long strokes.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then push the blunt irons of the belt buckle, according to what you need for opening the wound, and they should be such that the eyes can come out.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then scourge the sores that are underneath the skin of the genitals, as long as the white sores are hard and exposed on all sides.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then push your index finger into the genitals, between the first white sore that is underneath the skin of the egg and the second white sore.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and remove what is behind the egg, and between the second white sore; and then move your right hand inside the scrotum, and bring the first white sore up to your left hand, and lift the egg towards the abdomen with all the white sore.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister to stretch the arm upwards, and undo the one that is in front behind the elbow.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And if there is any intestine wrapped around the bone or hard white matter found, and if you discover anything of this kind, push it into the abdomen.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and push it into the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the kidneys; after the loin, then cut the joints that appear from the threads, until there are four threads left.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then gather the joints together in a cross-like manner and tie the syfac (the displaced tissue or organ) that we have mentioned is below the skin of the kidneys, with a strong thread of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then wrap the shoulders in cloth, and tie them with strips of fabric so that no vassals who nurse it can enter, unless an abscess cloth comes.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and make the knot according to the first knot long with two folds of that one, and after these two knots leave a space of about one finger's width under the keyhole for air to pass through.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and afterwards in the round shape that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the eye, as much as to corne it but not to break it, as we said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then apply moistened wool in oil, and place it on wounds, and bring the ligament as we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white parts as we have said are cauterized after incision, due to fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens often, and leave the ligament until it falls off by itself; if it does not fall off, heat with hot water, and apply what we have said until it falls off.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with another remedy, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never seen anyone dare to perform a cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done like a ramik who is assembled with the bladder, in this way that you tie the vessels after the incision lightly below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then press it in the middle, and treat the abscess of those who open it, until the vessels stop flowing; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes there comes rot in the groin, as we have said, and it opens the joints; and no internal organs are sent to the anus, and if any are sent, it is little, and it should be repaired every hour;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	Furthermore, if it remains too long in this place, the wound or phlegm grows, as long as internal organs are sent out;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	This occurs by the extension of phlegm in the groin, as we have said, because it is extended, then softened and inflamed the joints and opened;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	the patient lies down on his back between your hands, then strike the area of the swelling inflamed with a flatiron of three fingers width;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and pull out the pus that is under the skin which is swollen, then take the iron and place it on the apparent surface of the pus;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press the flatiron to the full depth of the abdomen, then cut the two apparent surfaces of the pus on top of the iron, and cut both;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then straighten the head (neck) and do not cover it with a cloth or extend the eye nor anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the ramie for the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then treat it with the treatment of wounds. And when you bandage the threads, if it becomes infected and treats the wound until it heals.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The cloth is compressed, without appearance in the wound, and the cauteries are more effective in this place and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin on the buttocks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin on the buttocks softens in some men, because the charms inside are softened and visible; and when one sees it is necessary to make the patient lie down on his back, and to strike the softened skin with the natural skin; then bring together two lips at a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess of the softened skin at 3 or 4 stitches firmly; then strike between the stitches, and the cure as with other wounds, until it heals, and close the hole with thread.
dou chastrement	the punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	1. Know that castrations are discussed in our law, and I do not wish to speak about it in this book; and it is not necessary but for two reasons: the first is that men in castration should respond when asked, and know the cure; and the second, because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, swine, and other animals. I say therefore that castrations are done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one that we do by attraction, make the animal sit in hot water until the genitals become softened; then grasp them with your hand, until they are restored and you no longer feel them.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two types: one type is like the figure of a woman between the two genitals, having hair and sometimes urinating in court; and another type is in women who have something above the penis as a rod and two genitals. And the treatment for both men and women is to cut the scrotum together and treat them like other wounds; however, there is no cure for men whose urine squirts through the skin of the genitals.
de la tentigene	Of the tenor (modern English)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The swelling (tumor) is a growth attached to the natural part, as long as it is ugly to see; and some women have such large ones as big as a hand, and that is the case. You must dye the superfluous part of the tumor with your hand or onions, and lightly cut it off; and do not go too deep, so bleeding does not occur, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and at another char (growth) that grows in the mouth of a woman, and it bursts out, and perhaps jumps away, and has the appearance of a cow, and for this reason they are called the "cow disease" by the ancients. If you must cut it off as we have said for the tumor, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	The erratic growth is a hardened or stone-like tumor on the surface of the body; and it is called "erratic" because it cannot be removed by simple cutting. When this kind of swelling arises in the body, it should be cut open with a knife until it is completely severed from its base; then take a hot iron or an emetic and cauterize (sear) the wound, so that the bad humors do not remain there and cause more pain.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	1. The erratic is when the nature of a woman is not perceived or is small; it can be natural at birth or accidental due to disease; it can be caused by the child being malpositioned, or from a subtle or large cephalic presentation, and it occurs fully in the womb, on the side, or underneath, or wherever it may be. They should be conceived and delivered, and the flowers should grow; this is recognized by observing the swelling of the belly. If the swelling appears near the hands or the navel, then hasten, and proceed as follows: place your two hands together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread out; then form the two hands, until the subtle cephalic presentation becomes round, and press the swelling; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the spot, and let the woman rest every day so that it does not heal. And if the cephalic presentation is hard and large, you must cut it with a spatula resembling the leaf of myrtle. If the swelling is of the afterbirth, suspend it at the navel and cut; have ready medicines to stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with much egg; then bring a large bandage, so that the wound does not heal; and in this way, it should be kept open, and bring a tent of dry linen; then cure other wounds until it is healed. And when in the womb, char nee appears, it must be covered as described above, unless it is an abscess enlarged. For the abscess enlarged that is in the womb, one should not try to touch or treat.
des emorroides	1. Hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Emorroydes are openings of veins that usually do not require treatment, and when emorroydes become old, they become threaded; and as we have said in the division, the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those that respond to cure. I say that emorroides and threaded ones, when they are fully grown in the womb, and they cannot be felt, can only be cured with iron. Those that are at the mouth of the womb, can be felt, are those that can be cured. Therefore, you must put the woman in a cold house, then remove the threaded one with tongs by its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicine over it to stop bleeding, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press her feet against the opening for an hour, then immerse it in cold water; and if bleeding persists, make her sit in a decoction of sumac bark and grape seeds and wild gale and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make one plaster on her back. If it bleeds, that is good. If not, make fumigating bags for the back and breasts without cutting; then take linen, wet it in plantain or marigold juice with old wine, and apply it to the place. And when the abscess settles, cure the place with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a small hard lump, so it must be covered as I have said for threaded ones; and then cure it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses in the womb
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.
