dou fremit	The trembling / shuddering
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formica is a small hollow place found between the body, and it travels deep inside;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes the shivering freezes the body, and it feels like death due to trembling, spreading throughout the entire body, more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a cane made from an ostrich feather or a strong goose quill and place it on the joint, until the purple circles encompass the joint all around;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand along the entire cane until you cover all around the joint and push it in, and harden the joint from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a cane made of iron or wood in the following shape, and be thin underneath and wide above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not perforate, because one must hold the breath and press; if you wish to cauterize, then cauterize the trembling, as is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster (enema)...
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make an enema of silver or arsenic, or melted beeswax or honey mixture; and sometimes they prepare small or large instruments according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, it is applied in the treatment of children who are weak and suffering, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cluster is either small or large, where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the head should be pierced within; and on one side there are two holes, and in the other one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	And let the stomach or man put the medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And between each hole, there should be space, then insert into these holes a strong thread of twisted cord in 10 or more layers, and bind the stomach like a goat's pouch.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicines are inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread in front, then cleanse (it); and this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicines not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the instrument with oil or egg yolk, or similar things, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the ministers press the patient's two hands together while he is completely visible, then take out the plaster and wash the patient's legs to the public area.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the medication seems to be working, squeeze as much as possible; and if it swells up all night long, it will be a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you plaster the patient with a belly disease of discharge, and the medication begins to heal quickly, continue to treat it until he is well.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are ulcerated or abscessed, whether they be the suppository as well, it should be of such subtlety as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the suppository with which the skin should be tightened:
des plaies	wounds  (plural of "plaie")
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you the treatments for hands and medicines, according to completion.  (The first two sentences are a summary of the previous section.)
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what kind they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Wounds are made by the thrusting of a spear, cutting with a sword and knife, or arrow or fist blow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	According to the parts of the body, such as a wound on the neck, or head, or chest, or stomach, or liver, and similar limbs.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will start with simple wounds of the head, for it will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or abscess and the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to arrow impact or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the healing of an abscess: if it makes pus from the head itself even though there is little blood from the wound, and the pus is on the contrary in the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and help the sick man to empty his body of wine and thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it doesn't want to heal, its flesh should be reduced, and it should not drink wine, nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And put on the wound if an abscess has come, cotton soaked in rose oil or stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, here I will say a little powder later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wounds have been moved by the wind, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like the size of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by suturing, as I will say about wounds in the abdomen, by suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is open to the bone, gaping and not holding together, bind it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore tough skin in place of hide.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And command the patient to eat coarse foods, such as boiled heads and cooked grain, like peas, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or leather putrefaction not on the bone, cover it completely and throw boiling water on it, then heal it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if an artery is in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without surgery, cut the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if the wounds are small and simple, the healing is easy: it is that you put this powder that hardens as soon as the flesh has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of the powder is: take a part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; four parts of live coal, and grind the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	apply the wound, squeeze it open, forming a hole, until it exhales well and unites with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, leaving it to heal by itself if it does not swell; for the medicine is not withdrawn until it heals.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at times this is done only with coal when neither incense nor dragon's blood is available, but the wound has not yet healed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the sore has moved the wound, indeed it has, do not put this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or powder made of barley flour with water and honey, until it stops flowing.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with subtle tweezers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you afterwards about the breaks of the head (or skull).
de la plaie dou col	About the wound of the neck (or throat)   (I am assuming that 'col' here means 'neck', but it could also mean 'throat'. The original French term is ambiguous in this context.)
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes or affects the neck and it is simple without any difference from that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the arteries are cut.   (The original French term 'col' is ambiguous in this context, meaning either neck or throat.)
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy than letting them heal on their own and not applying any restraints, for it harms the nerves and causes them to shrink.  (Assuming that 'col' means neck.)
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And place nothing cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be warm, such as hot water washed in sweet oil, and boiled in sweet oil as well.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	And other similar stones in the same way, and always moisten them.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it with strips, then heal it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and swollen with pus, pierce or incise them lower.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs, tie it off, cleanse it, and cauterize if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the spine of the throat is cut or the vein is preserved, so that the meat goes:   ...(rest of line missing)
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If the heart is located above the throat, and it does not touch the throat but is placed according to its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then allow it to progress and leave it for some days, then heal it with strong ointments until it heals.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	If the wound presses into the bone, open it.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are broken bones, break them all if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound heals.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And let the dislocation be reduced and aligned.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, cure as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from spear or knife.   --> Of the spear or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if bubbles rise from the wound; then know that the wound is fatal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it immediately nor bind it for the blood that dissolves will not stay in place.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	return to the patient's heart, and open him up.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	But apply an attracting ointment, and let it rest for two hours each time.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	And if you don't have an ointment, place a piece of dry cotton on the wound to draw out the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	Make the patient sleep on the wound for two or three days, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	If no spasm or bad tremor of the heart comes, nor any twitching of the entrails;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see the proper alignments, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Perform the cauteries and other treatments, until it is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	And if it cannot be healed, and it opens again, know that there is a fistula; cure it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword cut or knife, and it is simple (single), or deeper, or on the back, then treat what is in front of it.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, sew (it); if it is small, powder (it), and if it is embedded in the bone, and has split into fragments, whether it is an open wound or not, pull out the pieces if they are dislodged.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not dislodged, let the wound heal by itself, align the extractions (or treatments).
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, use similar judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The dislocation of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The dislocation of the abdomen is large, medium, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From a large wound, the intestines sometimes protrude, or the intestinal nerves, due to which the insertion occurs.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the sewing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Because one sets more on points the intestines if not put in gradually.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	As they swell quickly when they feel the cold, they return more to the points.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because it is better to treat a mid-sized wound, as one moves the intestines back to their place more than with other wounds.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the opening of the abdomen has four ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common joints occur at the abdominal joint
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the joints of other wounds on the body, and two more specific joints are common for other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Furthermore, they are more appropriate with the abdominal joint, and I will explain one of them:
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines protrudes,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	And great care is required when resetting [it], this is through one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or through the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the internal organs are swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Moisten a sponge or a piece of fine linen cloth with cool water only.
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	and you cook in boiling cypress and pine and spikewood.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and open the intestine as long as the inflammation is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes make this wine restraining, and it is boiled to soften to reduce inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling separate, if you moisten the intestines of cold or hot and ill-cooked water,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this means the entrance is closed to almost nothing.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut with an instrument used for coping with hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	And the first remedy is to reduce the fracture
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	but we should not cut it too much without necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it breaks through the neck and bends outward, then see its shape here:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines burst forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in its natural shape at its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, for this is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large and it is in the part beneath the abdomen,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	It is necessary that you make the patient lie down on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and raise their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part of the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	raise the head and the feet higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	And also if the hernia of the abdomen is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and you should know that the affected part should be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and in this way, you must apply what I say to both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use the appropriate remedy;
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then have between your hands a compassionate minister who anoints the entire wound with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common method of suturing,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and you take a needle or more, according to the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Then, leave some distance from the wound (i.e., thumb space), and insert an awl with one thick strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two skins with the two chisels of the spatula.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the two heads of the spatula together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	Then tie a double thread around the needle of .ij. parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	Then assemble the .ij. heads of the wound together.
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave .i. two inches of space, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	Then tie the thread as you have done with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing so according to what you need for the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is bound.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be medium-sized, neither too thin nor too thick.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	Subtle needles pierce the entire flesh, while the too large ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore they should be moderated.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and needles should not be pushed too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not pierce and open the wound before the seam.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	And then press the shoulders with needles, so they do not prick the patient while sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and place bands or cloths on the shoulders with needles to hold them in position.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	For he inflicts a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and you assemble the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of flesh together with a needle that has one thick thread in the middle.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have sewn all four pieces together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If you reinsert the needle at the part where you started, in the manner as we usually do with threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a small egg;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching binds [the wound] together;
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed a wound that a man had on his stomach,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than one palm wide (length),
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were two palm widths long (length),
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	The wound was within the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I will return the intestines after they have been outside for 24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	The wound was sewn shut for fifteen days, and healed, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the monks had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And do not heal it with ointment, for I am in one place where none is found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And apply old cotton to the wound twice a day, and wash it with water of honey until it heals.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and thrust it from the outside part up to within there.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the heart straight through, place the head of the splint or cost where you inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side of the inside out to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as pelters do fur.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the seam of one side, and return it from the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galen specifically calls,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	as one does who assembles the two parts naturally together.
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	And apply one of the heads of the lever to another head, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	thrust an awl or head of the mirror next to that place, and pierce it only there.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	leave the two heads of the lever;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the awl and pierce it from the outer side all the way to the inner part,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	2 heads of the shinbone;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other from the outer part to within, in 2 other shinbones that are on the opposite side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the muffled manner of stitching and the most common way.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen said this word, and no one can deny it;
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must sew the stomach with two needles, where there is thread on each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite, in the manner of those who sew purses.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	know that when the wound is within the stomach,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and the stitching in this part of the stomach is more difficult than other parts of the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is when you probe the fresh wound with all its blood, just as the surgeon has moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you replace the intestine, and its position; then place powder of arousing flesh on top.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	And if the arm has been moved, put some ointment on it until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	Pull out the thread and sew up the wound, and apply the marrow.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal the wound as with other cases, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, put on cotton wool immediately when it starts to heal;
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	And move it two times a day as long as it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need for any other medicine when the wounds are simple in many conditions.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound is affecting the main limbs,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	You must soak linen lightly in warm oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And place it around the ankles, beneath the knees;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or putrefaction in the belly, and this often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the cleansing with black vinegar softens, and especially when putrefaction reaches the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce through it, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine known as "jeun" cannot heal when it is punctured.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it is because of the inflammation in the veins that they are, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the herb jumps from the wound, place it back in the same way as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it becomes old or black, you must tie the part that is black so that blood does not come out from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	For there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then grip what is between the ribs.
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two heads hanging from the part below the wound toward the side to align the extraction when the arrowhead falls, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some people,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen that a man was wounded or stabbed with a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And it became swollen and turned into a fistula, and there was discharge and windiness from it.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied a remedy according to what I knew, and continued to refine it until he was healed, and the wounds closed up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw the wound close, I feared that the patient had an illness in his abdomen.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	But he had no ill health, but improved in better condition, and diet and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they said to any experimenters that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take firm hold of large testicles, then bring together the lips of the wound.
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the testicles have opened their mouth, place it on the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that its mouth protrudes.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then grip the head, and hold it so that it cannot dislocate.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then place another plier after it in this manner until the wound is completely closed.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head gets inflamed in the intestines, it causes no harm to the patient.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	And it can be tied with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal.
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread made of intestine which is rather fine.
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	then tie to the head of this thread (a) thin linen thread.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then insert the thread into the needle, sew the intestine, and straighten it in the incision;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching wounds is not beyond the path of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the great intestines, without remedy or health, it can only be done with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or when it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	All wounds or abscesses, when they heal, are universally referred to as "fistulas".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise, when it is healed and bursts open again.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	A fistula is according to the truth a hard and white nodule, where no pain is felt,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And it is as hollow as a bird's feather;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	Sometimes it jumps clearly upwards, and other times thickens;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes narrow, and other times quite wide;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	I have spoken of wounds in the division of injuries, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh;

ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	For because there is hard flesh within and above the lips, do not let it grow flesh.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	For there is too much pus.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	The loins are swollen, and the matter is of poor quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	The medicine is not good for the treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	For, because corruption is a form of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	For, due to the property in that area, digestion is slow, health is delayed, and it naturally swells.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	there are veins or bones;
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, the signs, and the treatments with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must tell you the remedy for a fistula made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from the veins, arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in one of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it affects the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all these fistulas are of grave illness, and there is only labor and ignorance in them.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	And if there is any fistula that does not reach up to the level I have said, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you investigate it, if you take a tent of bee wax or iron, if the fistula is straight, push it through.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, search for a thin reed stick,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the reed bends around the twist;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	And if the fistula (a small abnormal passage or cavity) at the hand has been torn apart, you cannot find it again with probing,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	If the hernia (protrusion of an organ or tissue through a weak spot in the surrounding muscle or connective tissue) has come out through one of the openings,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because moisture is so short from one opening to another, and it should be cleaned.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then carefully probe it to the best of your ability to determine if there is bone or nerve involved and whether it is fully closed.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	And ask the patient carefully about the pain they feel when you press on it with your hand, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	And when you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein.
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	In any of the places that I have told you, if the edge is cut according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And bone should be removed from the fracture and the corrupt cartilages that are within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	And then the cure until it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well penetrated straight through, it is necessary that you close it completely, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put dampened tents filled with medicine into the fistula, and push them up to its head,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	As long as the medicine corrodes the surplus that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then put warm bandages on the healthy flesh, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this means, then cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, break it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerves do not burden or main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, wait until all the corruption is removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it with soothing salves until it heals completely;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	if it does not heal and bows again as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	Know that you are not yet at the fountain:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	cover and remain as long as you are at the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	remove all corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	if it is in such a state, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that corruption is too far advanced, that you cannot reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy but to let nature take its course.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corruption, and you can extract it with pliers.
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if it can be extracted with one tool.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there are many bones, draw them all out, do not leave any of them.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	cover and moisten and wrap the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something warm and moist over the wound,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	And let [the joint] be surrounded by tendons around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And then [it will be] easier to move the bones.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	let [the bone] remain until all the blackness is removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part corrupting down to the bone:
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to be covered entirely up to the corruption, and then heal it until it heals over.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I will tell you about a fistula that happens to one man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man of around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to a cause that came from within his body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matter came to his leg, and it was burst out with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it further.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the fools, through their folly, overdid (the incision) so much that the abscess opened
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they dug too much into matters, and it became a fistula, and much pus came out that everyone bent down with moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many fools put cures on it for two years but there was no healer skilled in medicine.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called to see the leg and the medicines with which they were treating it,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And those who run through wounds with great haste;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the bodies of the young men turn red, and they have a yellow complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I set up a tent at one of these wounds, then searched for all the wounds,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	And I found that the one was coming towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I therefore hastened, and cut into one of the wounds until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it corrupt and rotten, and the corruption reached the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I considered that there was no other corruption in the bone than what remained;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to heal the wound with salve for a long time, but it would not close.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then examine [the area] and uncover the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And find the continuous corruption in the bone, and I cleaned it, and then left it open, and then tried to mend the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not join it altogether as I wrapped around a palm of the bone, and pulled it too hard.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	Then I restored it with medicines; and it healed and mended quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	And it should not begin work again except due to the weakness of the patient, who cannot endure,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For due to the blood evacuation it often happened, but he was completely healthy,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	And there grew a hard cartilage in the place of the bone, and it was well-placed and had no harm or opposite effect anywhere, neither at arrival nor at coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken at any location of the body, it should be treated as follows:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a splint, and hold it at the open end of the broken bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command anyone that it should be extended upward;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another thicker splint of linen on top of the skin covering the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And extract the corrupt flesh beneath the skin of the head,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and expose the flesh on the surface where you want to be, so that the bone does not prick the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a splint or a flat piece of wood underneath the bone to protect the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	It must be as much as possible to see and feel the corruption, and be checked again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then put a splint underneath; afterwards, heat it with a hot iron.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and let the splint be from one part of the corruption to the other, and let the splint be the length of the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is at the joint, strike the corrupted joint and the bone that it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy but to cover [the affected area].
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if corruption is in the end of the hand or the foot, it is a very difficult matter.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	But it is necessary that you investigate this corruption, how it opened.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways you can, but do not harm the vein or the nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And know that the incision tool and the saws for covering these bones are numerous, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for that reason, it is necessary to equip each type of work with its appropriate tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	Choose the instrument that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The cheeks may swell due to something inside or outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have remedied this corrosion through the use of medications, but they do not help at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that member up to the place where the corrosion comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient may perish from this through death or through a greater ill-will due to the failure of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black as if it were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	And then comes the blackness, afterwards goes the corruption of member to member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	It takes hold of the whole body; if you hasten to cover it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if this is by the bite of certain venomous creatures such as sea scorpions and snakes and similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is at the head of the neck, if you cover it, do not give it any space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, strike at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	If it reaches the forearm, strike at the edge; if it passes the edge, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no use in applying remedies outside of its quantity of virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and act accordingly when the corruption comes or is putrefied: if it comes in the first joint, strike after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or falls, cover all of it;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it goes up in the leg, cover at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, there is no remedy for the sick but death.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the method of covering or caring for the limb is such that you bind it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	extend one minister one of the lower straps, and another minister the other strap upward.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you cut open the flesh between the two straps one thumbwidth wide, so that the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you cover or bandage it, putting on one side a linen cloth, so that the wound does not touch healthy flesh.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And comes another injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes when you work, then cauterize the area quickly,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put some restraining powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then tie the limb with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it heals.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to one person in the leg:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a dark swelling that looked like it was burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corruption first appeared in his thigh bone, until it covered the entire thigh.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the bones see corruption, he strikes them with copper [instrument] and makes them healthy.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards corruption or decay of the hand returned to him, and it came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed him in restorative things after the body's cleansing, but the corruption could not stop.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and you request that I cut off his hand, but I do not want, for I have hope of restoring the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	And also doubted if I were to amputate his hand, he would not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the virtue of man was weak; and he lost all hope, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and if I strike his hand with a sword, it will be well (healed).
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have not thought of anything else except that this can be done differently if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess sometimes appears in a charred area and remains for so long that it causes a large swelling of boils.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then they run and pierce, and the boil bursts, and the place becomes visible, like a wound of a knight;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above it is as thin as a piece of linen unraveled;
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not reach the bone or the nerve, and such illness is called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends all the way to the bone in depth, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cook should be such that you cut through the entire hide, and in the same way when it is subtle, like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not disappear due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have a suspicion that the flesh is hardening, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with pus, cure it with clisteria (a medicinal enema):
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	check if the breasts are swollen and the boil that is in it has a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then apply Egyptian medicinal clisteria (enema) made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take asafetida, oil, and litharge equally, and cook them in one vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and thickens to the consistency of honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take according to your need from it, and make it into an ointment and a syrup,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and apply the poultice to the breast, and compress the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine inside for 2 hours, then draw it out by pulling.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is drained of pus;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes cleansed with water and ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, take vine ash, pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then let it bleed, and anoint it with ointment, until you know that the breasts are well healed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	if the patient cannot bear it, nor Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if you anoint it with water and honey or a little powdered gallstones.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you anoint it with honey and sweetened wine, where the honey has the property of purifying and cleansing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	And the wine makes the blood thin;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have confidence that the breasts are well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the suppository made to stimulate chyme in him,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And you shall prepare an emulsion of pennyroyal and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	and you shall coat it with certain medicines and liniments, of which I have spoken about their properties or treating the liniments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	And if the breast wound is small, and the linen cloth of the liniment cannot enter.
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	If a wound caused by a small knife is large, put an Egyptian ointment plaster over it.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment, as long as it is large;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, cut and leave one to two leagues or the lancet can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the hernia that bulges is above, press it down or lower than it.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is fully drawn, do not let it release the arrow.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	arrange it in such a manner that the bow bends to its lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the boil is fully formed, do not let it burst.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you see.
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	arrange it in this manner: let the boil run easily downwards, and do not leave anything of the boil.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	take consolidating medicine for putting on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	And stretch over it a linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then press the force against the wound of the breast with something wider than the first (pressure).
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	Then anoint it softly with another cloth according to the size of the wound,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and lay it on the wound of the breast to align the bone, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And he who is on the breastbone, often opens for removing the break,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	knows what comes from the break, if it's poisonous or infected or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	takes care whether the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	when your medicine has been applied in this way and you see the nature that rises on the breastbone.
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	If you know that breasts swell up, then approach them with care;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and in the morning or at midday, when you are about to open the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change one bandage for another, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	If the breasts are swollen and do not improve after several days, know that they will not swell further.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons attack after a long time, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the healing approaches. For there are people whose wounds heal slowly, and those who make it worse.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if a badly digested bowel moves through the chest after many days, know that breasts do not move.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are slow to grow, and are swollen, apply drying medicine with moist substance and dry qualities.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	As an ointment defined, for it contains much vitriol, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take ointment defined, made with rose oil, and rosehips of equal substance in quantity.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and apply it; and the same made in a more cooked state, swollen,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when ointment defined is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	Take myrrh, aloe, and incense, grind them together, and sprinkle the powder on honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	Then place one cloth and lay it on the chest, and sometimes administer an aromatologist long oil.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily, which is as fine as flour and cinnamon.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make powder and put it on the honey that I mentioned, and use.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the patient is prolonged (i.e., not healed), and is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	therefore learn that corruption is imminent, and it creates pressure on the bone, or on hard members, or ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of this fistula, as we have said before, does not heal the patient.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess at the nailbed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pancreatic abscess is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or under the toe, or by chance it may arise in other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes inflamed and no care is taken, an abscess forms.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they cut and throw boils until they reach the root of the nail, and by chance they may cut it entirely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And comes the corruption to the bone, until it brings pain that smells, and the head is wide open, and the color is drained away.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help at all.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	Then you must cut into it. Remove all the excess that remains from the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are very great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and when the nail follows the flesh closely, and it begins to swell and crack,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	you must put the radish under the nail to prevent the flesh from touching;
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And raise it up, and strike the flesh gently and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place on top of the remaining flesh the remnant of the medicine that is burning and corrosive to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with ointment until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	If the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw out pus, because as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the thumb bent, strike it with a hammer as previously mentioned,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wounded, broken, and causing great pain, it must be drained first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then strike the nail with a sharp spatula in a transverse cutting motion from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And be careful that the cut does not reach down to the flesh below the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If it happens, place something on top to alleviate the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deaf man's hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The patient must cauterize who is born in some men's hands by chance, it is all fleshly.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone or nail, and occasionally there is a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born in the root of the joint, but rather in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one who is born in any nail does not grow out,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And if one is born at the join of the thumb, by chance he remains mute;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of that who is fat is light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the length in its root like a broad spoon.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	If one is born at the root of the join, he is difficult to cure; keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or about to die, it is necessary that you cut the cartilage roundly up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate saw for this, then cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same sores that come at the joints come together by birth, or by injury of a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary to cut the sore, so that it can heal according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or damp cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	and you put thin pieces of wood between them so that the joints are glued together, as necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	In the same way, if any of his hands comes with the palm, then strike that joint as necessary.
Des vils	Of people
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large, swollen vessels filled with melancholic excesses, which come into many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it happens more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must sometimes administer purge of bile, and then let it flow from the basilica (biliary duct).
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is in two ways: one is to hit them, and the black blood is drained out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is to open a vein and let it bleed completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision method is as follows: first make an incision on the leg with very hot water until the flesh softens.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then hold the patient's leg from above the calf to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then open the vein in one, two, or three places, of a wide size,
