puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then draw and let out the black blood from the one end to the other, as much black blood from it as the strength of the patient can withstand.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and instruct him to bind himself with meat colored black.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, it is beneficial for the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The swelling of it [the affected area] is as follows: measure the limb of the patient, if there is much hair on it,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then place it in water, and raise the limb in warm water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have water, heat it on fire, and then press it against the vein along the length of the thigh or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then scrape the skin with a knife at the edge, and cut open the vein from both sides, until it appears when you feel it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And one sees it red and black, and when it enters or skin resembles a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then push the rod inside until it reaches the skin, and then pierce it gently.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then strike it in another place four fingers' breadth away; then peel the skin over the vein as far as it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then tie the rod to the vein, as you did, and pierce it again at another angle, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then take another size, or more if needed, then warm it, and apply to the base of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then straighten and warm up to the second size; then cut it piece by piece until it comes out completely, and apply.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	And if you cannot draw it out and lift it, push an awl with a single strong double thread through it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	Hold the awl straight and draw it out, then turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep it from bruising, for if it bruises, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it, place on the wound a cloth dampened with vinegar and rose oil; and let it heal until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the wound is contracted, twisted, and rolled together, not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	Then you must cut it obliquely, but do not cover it; and draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to pierce the vein is curved and does not cut, it should not pierce the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curve, for if it is subtle, it would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	From the civil vein (a blood vessel)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is opened in legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in ground where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And sometimes it grows elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to the corruption coming from under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	if it comes inside the body and spreads, open between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	If the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg with a very large inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then change the joints, and start the vein to come out, as a root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder is open, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of wood from 6 to 8 inches long and bind it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wood on the leg, and every time it comes loose from the wound, wrap it again around the wood and bind it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut a part of it and roll up the remaining, do not cover it at its root until it comes out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, cause an abscess and pus or a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of that, it must be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	sometimes this vein is about five fingers long or ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And one man came to me, whose length was ten feet, and when you cut it, push a pound or a hole through it, and pierce it all the way down,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything inside is emptied out; and bring the matter within it to its place, and apply the medicine in the form of poultice for three days, then treat it as an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes with this vein, many raindrops come out, and especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or hand,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes much from ruptures, and where it jumps around; cure it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From worms that are born between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it often occurs in cows.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body swelling and subsiding,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	It sends [the patient] great pain from member to member as it desires, until it breaks the skin or jumps forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	It is poisoned by corruption of some humors, such as those that come towards and resemble snakes, worms, and parasites or the stomach;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its malice, for when it goes through the body, it ascends to the head, and reaches the eye;
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance, oil enters [the body] and is destroyed; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you want to cure and draw it, one can only force it when it wants to go out:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Therefore, you must tie the loin (intestines) above and below with a strong, narrow cord:
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	Then press above and pull out forcefully, and if the head is full in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If you cauterize with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm that it does, is that it runs the oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold a bellows under it, then strike above, and draw it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and the patient must use a bodily cleansing of medicinal solutions to remove harmful humors;
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And if they are spoiled with meat poisoning.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind-sickness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "wakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it moves from member to member; as I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And afterward, it began to rise like a worm towards the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, as hot iron when it is cut from one piece to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain spread from that place and pierced into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little while after it runs through the whole body, until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I saw that it would repeatedly turn around the body.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly surprised how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this kind of disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Indeed, I had seen many cases where the pain moved from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	But I had not wanted it, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins exposed.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this, the constrictions of wind appear;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not apply to those who are healthy and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you wish to cure this disease, and the patient feels this pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	press down hard on both sides and then push upwards until the windiness is constrained to its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the spot; if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If the treatment for those suffering from windiness is like poison pills or Serapion pills, and similar ones.
Des saiettes	If the treatment for those suffering from windiness are arrows or needles.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows or needles come in different types, depending on their shapes and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity among them is that there are some with large points, small ones, rounded, and pointed.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two joints, and of those with tongues, and of those where there are parts or fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And the dislocation in any limb occurs in two ways: either in the principal member, the head,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	If the dislocation occurs in any of these members, then the signs of death that I will tell you hereafter will be apparent to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	It is necessary for you to be cautious about the extraction of this arrow, for many deaths follow in various situations.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if this bad sign does not appear and the arrow is not fully inserted, draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when an arrow pierces the bone and the socket that is above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when the eye becomes cloudy and swollen, and inflamed and red around it, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And by chance, it may occur without force from the nostrils or ears; and by chance, speech and voice may be lost.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And from the wound white moisture jumps out, resembling pus, and also jumps like boiling oil.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If this sign appears, refrain from the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces is that it is close to the left breast, and it feels like it has been stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance, the seventh becomes mute like hair, and in black blood it bleeds, and there comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, one can doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that pierces the body is when a scab does not rise from the wound and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, breathes heavily and seeks warm air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bed of the sick person, it has pierced the sides; and he spits a large amount of saliva and feels great pain and breathes heavily; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead or stomach falls out by chance, anything from the undigested flesh may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrowhead or abdomen falls out and something from the intestinal tract jumps out, there is no hope in the treatment nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrowhead falls into the bladder and urine jumps out and spills, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the hand, arm, neck, shoulder, backbone, waist, hips, legs, and those similar, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason you should do something else.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man that an arrow struck or pierced the root of his neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear and it was harmless without any damage.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I played a game with an arrow that struck in the oil sac under the paper,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was inserted, and it could not reach beyond its point towards the bone.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, all one piece of light iron without ears; the patient recovered, and no harmful accident occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	It passed an arrow through the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was a barber, and I was skillful enough to pull it out, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And take an arrow out of one man who was shot or stabbed, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, pulled it out, and had no bad outcome.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	If one man is shot or stabbed, and the wound is sewn shut;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow remained inside it, and did not change its natural position.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor was found detrimental in any of its natural workings.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And a man, who got an arrow in his face, and the wound became closed.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and it remained thus without suffering great pain for a long time, and many similar things happened.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And treat an arrow wound in a knight of the king who was struck within the neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly inclined towards the right side; and the arrow was completely buried.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned to the treatment after it happened seven days ago. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I stretched it with a fine tent and felt no pain.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrowhead.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied the plaster attractant and digestif because the wounds did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the arrowhead of the wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I place the plaster on the wound for many days, and straighten the fracture directly, and keep the patient for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he feels the arrowhead inside his neck for one day; then tell him.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put a corrosive medicine on the wound by hand, until it is opened.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and probe it, and feel the head of the arrow that adheres to the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I align in the opening of the wound with that ague medicine, until the head of the arrow becomes visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and he passed well beyond the four-month term.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I cut open the wound that I had punctured with the pincers, and it refused to heal from one side or the other.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not cease to refine and devise ways of instruments, until I took the pincers well made for a whole day.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to its form that will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I follow it and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the judges decide that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restore it, and the wound heals, and the patient is completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	And I have told you about the quality of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you apply your remedy to this (condition), I do not say that you should not do otherwise, because the books cannot completely grasp everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters comprehend little things and things that are present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	True nine times out of eleven, and nine times are the instruments, in the examination of things strange that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not enter into limbs where they are thrust except according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Or by what side they enter, or from another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out where it enters is an arrow penetrating into the flesh, and jumps out occasionally.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh is swollen around it and the opening is closed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is driven into the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, pierce it all around with a fine needle, until the joints around it are opened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the skull bone, and goes to one of the brain ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said to the patient: do not drain it at all, but let it heal evenly after several days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow reaches the heart, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is inserted only into the bone and does not reach the heart,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	The patient remains for some days with no bad accidents, if the device to draw it is used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply inserted and cannot come out, then administer tourniquets around it, as I told you before; then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is placed back in the body where it cannot be seen, you should seek it with all your might;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, you must draw it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow prevent it,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein if the wound is large enough;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	And pull the arrow out if you can, and if it has ears in the arrow as it is,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	and remove the foreign body that is embedded in two parts into the muscle as far as you can,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrow's ears until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	be careful not to break the arrow, but try to pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, pull down the leg to the joints, then draw, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding prevents you from performing the extraction, bring forth what we have said in its chapter for treatment;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and use devices as you can pull out the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For it is the greatest aid there can be, and if you cannot do it, have it done as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or it opens something of it, or the skin is swollen around it, as one can see or feel clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then cut through it, as long as the tweezers can take hold, and then pull it out; if it is not possible to do so now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it [the dislocation] is held within the bone, you should turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, you should leave it for a while, and then continue the extraction until it comes forth.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is of an arrow shaft, push it all the way through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it fell and you want to administer a poultice, then administer one poultice made with cheese;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; then force it through.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is entangled (or caught) in the hair, apply force to the instrument, causing the pointed end to penetrate and ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touching (or lodged in) something, you should cut all the flesh around the area where the poison is present, if possible.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls or pierces in the belly, bladder, side, or kidney, and it is nearby, and you can cover over it, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And keep from covering the vein and the nerve, then extract it, then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tweezers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the boil is also like a bird's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push the point of the arrowhead in this manner:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tweezers for pushing and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Incisions of the common body cavities
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Incisions for draining are 31, of which there is a head of 16
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: Two pans that are after the ears, which are called "double herb"
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins which are in each eye, called "aspirates".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	The vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two tendons which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins that are in the upper lip above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly bled are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle part is called "fast," and it consists of the cephalic and basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And common people call it "vein of the abdomen," and it is above the liver.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	This is the one that is used for bloodletting, which opens clearly at the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the savatal is the vein which is between the auricular and annular [bones], and it has two rain(s).
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are four veins: one is under the calf of the left side.
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphenous vein which is at the wrist of the right side; and the vein called "nisse," which is in the wrist of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg there are 3 veins beneath those [veins].
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The veins that follow the ears help the ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the vein, as I say to you, are such that you rise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	As long as the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Then, where you feel the pulse beneath your neck, press firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lance, and push it through the vein to the bone, then withdraw your hand along the entire vein,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Cut through the skin and vein with two blows, and make the blood come out until you see it.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then hold and bind it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the temples, is worth to migraine old-age people,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And it is also sooty and inflammation of the eyes, and to the heart of cold eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient stretches out his neck, until two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse beneath your thumb, and then examine it carefully;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the finger to the upper part of the vein on your index finger, and push the lancet underneath;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Lift the vein up, strike it (as you have done in two other veins), and draw the blood as necessary.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form (the incision) carefully, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their dressing and extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the forehead vein is worth as much as the healing of the head vein for facial diseases such as migraines and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality is such that the patient stretches his neck while turning, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "excavator", whose shape is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let blood flow according to the amount you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then separate the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is sealed and not open one time with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	In addition, the flames should not be too sharp; and obliquely, because the bone is near, and by chance the flames may break when they are fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The veins of the two eyelids assist in the eyes, and in the tear duct, and in the nostrils, and in the ear in oil, and in facial diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their veins is such that the patient can strain his neck by twisting some rope or cord, as previously mentioned.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then, make it healthy, and let the incision be across [the affected area], a bit long and wide, for there is no flesh therein.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the fire is thin, perhaps it may break; then correct the blood flow, as much as you need, and then cover it with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The incision of the vein near the neck is good for ague, scrofula, and fevers caused by corruption.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as well as migraines and redness that come from the face, especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the qualities of the purgative are that the patient compresses their neck, then holds their genitals with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a subtle long flame, and thrust it between the two nostrils in the space,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well in this way, and the arteries will soon begin to bleed;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too far forward, make the wound cauterize according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is soon healed.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of fire (cautery):
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salve of two kinds (guides) helps in the strengthening of the sinews, and at the beginning of inflammation, and in many diseases, and in stopping abscesses, and in corroding, and in sores, and in ulcers.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the salve is such that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient lie on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then let the vein heal along its length for a short distance, then draw out the blood moderately, as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then reset (the dislocation) on the other side, then undo the ligament, and hold the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Do not squeeze (the wound); let it heal by itself until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On the treatment of boils
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of mouth boils also helps with cold in the mouth and corruption of the gums, and cuts and sores around the mouth.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the salve are to make the patient sit before you, and hold its neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the jaw, and look at the two veins, one on the right jaw and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are recognized by being black, and by the small black veins around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Then take one or the other (the shoulder), and if you do not know them, and you are uncertain,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then take the largest one of each pair (shoulders), and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the incision under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The incision under the tongue helps after the cephalic incision, and it is used for the treatment of throat diseases, eye diseases, and mouth diseases.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of a blood-letter are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up the tongue, and looks under each side at a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	And so both sides, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins along the side from which blood-letting is commonly done are done according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or by puncturing with a sharp point made of myrtle wood or fine olive oil, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are wide and fine according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It must be necessary to open large veins with visible thick blood, and those containing thick and troubled blood:
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	This is the form of the olive oil lamp:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointedly subtle, and is for healing subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The healing of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and neck, and chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the healer to heal promptly, and to drain the artery that is beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	If he pierces the artery, and blood flow comes out, it should be stopped, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame must not be pressed, but cut as with a saw.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open naturally, you must force it and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want any wound from him, or you heal in its place the vein in the arm: it opens naturally.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the cup to the flame anneal, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the wound, then you must also stretch out the arm and touch the place where you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the place with a sign, tie up the arm, and heat the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery; avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise high as a child's urine, and the limb is red and thin, know that this is not from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Then place your finger firmly on top, press down for a long time, then cut off the limb where it turns pale repeatedly, as this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave the arm alone and do not move it, the patient should be afraid and not move it until it is healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the limb is not bleeding and it pains you, and there is no medicine present, then cut open the artery if it opens, because the head of the limb will retreat; stop the bleeding from the limb.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bark of fustic, cut it, and take one half of it and bind it tightly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it does not stop bleeding, that's fine; if it does not, heal it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stoppage of bleeding is not necessarily helpful in many situations due to the small size of the wound and the thickness of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above, and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the lord must turn it by the nerve that is below, and if it pricks too deeply, and finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient suffers pain, and there is no healing.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens widely many times, and if it does not open in any person due to its subtlety, then you must anesthetize the area with the instrument; and press the nerve as hard as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The pain of the skull helps, which draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to anesthetize by pressing on the olive oil or myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins because there is no nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Therefore, one must seek the easier joint, and not worry if it is necessary to do it for the first time, and one can repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes joints swell in some men, which requires it for the first time, but do not worry about it.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of urine is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about urinating is that urination serves only for maintaining health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And the incision should be made in one of the four veins that are known as: cephalic, femoral, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should incise at the beginning of the thigh, in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one should incise on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The administration of medicine for diseases has no fixed hour, but when it is needed, day or night, in every hour and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not advisable to treat children under the age of 14 or a woman carrying child for less than four months up until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old people over sixty years old should not be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to be treated in any manner, it is necessary that the intestines should be cleansed with a mild cleansing agent.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If much filth is retained, to the extent that veins do not expel intestinal waste from the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor is he healthy who is excessively salted with meats, or drunk, to such an extent that he is feverish or dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if diarrhea occurs after a colic attack, vomiting, abdominal distention, multiple abortion of a woman, excessive labor, watching, and fasting, or total loss of strength due to the weapon or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the bodily fluids, if it is swollen, by means of food and drinks and medications, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and let the blood flow from the vein on the affected side, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep yourself that day from labor, exertion, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And bind and hold the patient, raise the surgeon's hand higher than the patient, and rub the arm 2 or 3 times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then gently pull the ligament above, as when it is too tight or narrow, it cannot be corrected without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with hands until the veins swell, and feel them to ensure they are swollen.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	and then wet the surgeon's hand with a little oil, then place his fingertip of his left hand on the vein below the area where he will lance it.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	That the vein does not open nor break at the incision.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like ropes in a sieve, and some are filled with venosity,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For when heat is applied, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with some of them.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if they open a vein, the wound is too narrow, so the surgeons should be mindful of this.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If it opens the first time, that's fine; but if not, restart from the same place or shortly thereafter, unless the limb is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	If the limb is swollen and the patient becomes fearful, wait one or two days and do not tie up the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case pus ulcers arrive, they should not enter baths or water; then start treating the wound again if it pleases them.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the perforation is small or the wound subtle, and you doubt that it does not bleed as much as you see, trust in the perforation itself entirely with all the flame directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	Work it a little hastily, so that the flesh is inflamed; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh inflamed, do not start draining it, and apply a little oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil is healed.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And so administer the oil of lard in every wound that you cleanse the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And similarly use treacle and boil it when putting it on the wound; if it becomes too thick, thin it.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	If an abscess becomes large, which happens many times, similarly when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, place a damp sponge soaked in vinegar and a little hot oil on it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place for some days without any black or green discoloration, it does not matter.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh that has been steeped in calcament, mastic, or similar substances.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often abscess and appearance appear at the healing of the basilica: place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to pressure from the hand, then that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything above what has been said, because by chance without the artery; but let it be one plug of dry material to harden the place, then cure it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out blood from each person according to the quantity of its strength and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is filled and hollowed out, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed a little and often, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bloodletting is safe from the corruption of blood and the compression of nerves, and it is more effective than long bloodletting or wide bloodletting.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body needs to be purged, it is necessary to give soft bread with pulp of pomegranates; if he is hot, bleed him four or five times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of cold complexion, eat before purging soft bread in syrup, or syrup of honey aromatic with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	If he has diarrhea during purging, after the flow of blood, it is necessary that he drinks broth of meat and a subtle fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And use other things as we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to dislocate someone's arm and then relocate it at another time, when it has been weakened by much bleeding, it should be done little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to dislocate someone's arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong heart, should wait 9 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another part, should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood inside the body which is already overheated and causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw a large quantity and widen the opening until it can pass through.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	and reward all the conditions of health, place your hand on top of the foot when it is healthy, so that death does not come in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when the healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary that you dislocate the arm again, draw blood a second time, and the wound is closed, but you should press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, extend the arm forcefully, for it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until it heals the second time; or you pierce it with the point of the flame, until the congealed blood that was in the vein escapes.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place one piece of fresh linen in boiling water and press lightly on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if a vein has burst, let it be and do not compress it until the abscess is pacified.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If it requires drawing blood a second time, draw it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is safer to use instead of the one in the neck because it is composed of different vessels.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	The way to draw blood is that the patient pushes their hand into boiling hot water until the vein turns red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it should be tied moderately, so that the vein appears well, then keep pressing gently across, neither too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the incisions wide, and press well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be extracted, place the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow out in the hot water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not plunge the hand into hot water, as it puts it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this vessel is safer than all other vessels, for there is no artery or nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The swelling of the vein of the right hand is worth all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	press the hand, and put in hot water until the vein swells up if you can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	If the wound is transverse, and if you close it completely, it will cause no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, for the nerves are all exposed under skin.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then put your hand in hot water, if the wound is frozen and cannot be extracted.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as needed, put oil and linen over the wound to heal quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purification of the hand on the left side is beneficial for the disease of paralysis, and it should be done in the same way as I told you concerning the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The purification of the sole is beneficial for all the diseases that are beneath the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the womb, retention of flow (menses), disease of the kidneys and thighs, and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of its purification are that the patient should immerse his foot in hot water and rub it on the vein until it bleeds,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And lay it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many rivers.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Then, lay it on the larger river or at the ankle, which flows more easily.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you lay it on the leg below, watch out for nerves that are beneath it, and lay it through just as in cutting; let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the leg cannot be extracted, place it in the water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the blisters require treatment for the first time, start with the second one slightly above, because the area is salted;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and proceed with the same method for the sole of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The salted area of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its blister is worth the pain of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its blister are that the patient immerses it in water and squeezes above the ankle four fingers' width.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	Otherwise, the vein will not open; and if it opens, heal it in all possible ways that you can, and by crossing over.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better to close it, because the place is empty, and it is much more vulnerable to hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't bind it, there will be no blood to stop its opening or the top of the foot, and beware of nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Make as much pressure on the blood as you can see, then untie the string, and place cotton on it and bind it again; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	From the blisters (of cupping)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters (of cupping) are made from horns or goat's horn, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by bleeding and drawing blood, or without bleeding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this type of cupping that does not involve bleeding is done in two ways: either it is done by fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And the cupping that involves bleeding is made in twelve parts of the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	The patient is either completely unconscious (asleep) or dead, the others are moved to the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two more in the sides of the neck; and the bladder underneath the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the bladders of the two shoulders; and the bladders above the ankles;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the bladders in the two arms; and the bladders in the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the boils of the two shins; and the boils do not bleed, unless from small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason, do not open them at all, as one does with bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered in any case, neither with hot water nor heated water, in any disease that comes from excess, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	If it is necessary for diseases to bleed, or according to custom, we will administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and at every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to ventose, have heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and those who find swelling and redness in their belly, head, neck, and darkening of the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who have a drop of blood in their mouth and have swollen tongues, and exude blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if [there are] some who think, and see by no blood or abscesses or death or similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When we see these signs and especially when it is in the month [of the disease], we order to bleed after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purging of the muzzle helps with the gritting of the teeth ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the entire body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this ventosation is in the location of the head of the cervical (spine)
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it should not be used by those with cold constitution or who have scabies, for it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore the elderly should not use it, nor those with head colds diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become obtuse, and for this reason, the blister should be placed a little lower due to the risk of becoming obtuse.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventosation is placed on the neck at the base of the skull and in the basilica, and for that reason it is useful for the stretching of the bones.
