et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to cut through the channel of the vertebra, and immediately, and to be filled up.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	It must be pushed gently, for if it holds too firmly, it causes obstruction or blockage in the belly or in the heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventosations at the two ribs of the neck are useful for headaches, migraines, strangulation and pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it should be in the position of the basilica's sacred place; and you must instruct the lord to press his hand to put it, not strike the artery, and no bleeding should come.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are good for mouth disease and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it should be in the positions of the two cheeks.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations of the shoulders are good for disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the sides are as valuable as three veins from the arms.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the lord not to cut too deeply, for the veins are naked of flesh, and it knows beneath dark and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The boil on the buttock is effective for treating hemorrhoids at their base and diseases underneath, and it should be large and made of lard, as it needs to be well-drawn; and if it were subtle, it would break; and in that case, it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The boils on the legs open widely because they draw blood from the whole body, and they are effective for treating old pains in the joints, such as those of the knees and ankles, and they remove the flower; and they are located between the shins and the knees, and the ankles, and although they weaken the body after long use, they bring down pus in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the boil is that you put it first and apply it promptly, press it evenly, and continue this action until you see the place turning red and swelling, and opening the redness of blood; then wait and put the boils back, taking care in the disposition of the body, as there are those with soft skin and clear pores: it is necessary to cut only once, and it is necessary to make wide and deep wounds, and a little superficially.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the limb is thick, it should be cut twice: the first time to make a path for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the limb is very thick, it should be cut three times; and when we want to draw out the thin blood, we only need to prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	If we want much blood, we should encourage it frequently; and if the limb is thick, we pierce deeply and let the veins be punctured suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and are narrow-pored, that you anoint the joints of the swellings with stimulating and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this case, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil from the seeds of cucumbers.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in a fever, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluidity is large and cold, take amat oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and others like it.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one to whom you are applying hot iron has wide and large pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it should be washed after the application with rose water, or cold water, or water of morello cherries, or water of gourd, or water of pottery, or any similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And one who has much moisture, if he rises from bed, should do so with asafetida or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And one with large superfluidities rises with old wine or grape juice, or the infusion of anise or chamomile, or similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And it is not advisable to bleed with a cupping glass before bathing nor in the bath, but an hour or two after bathing, and one should not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he urinate, when he should be bled and after being bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	Watch the one who bleeds is bilious, and if he is not enough or too inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It is necessary for him to take cold things, such as raw pomegranates, endives and lettuce leaves; and similar items.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and also consume purgatives, meat of the chestnut, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold constitution, should take honey syrup, fragrant moderate wine (between old and new), purgatives, and also consume parsnips, small birds, and young birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	On the day he will vomit, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give some men sometimes triticale or muscatel before swelling, or after, for strengthening the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And thin the blood of those who are hot, but it is not necessary that those who are cold drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The boils placed on wounds are those placed on the liver, spleen, gout, stomach, intestines, and hernia, as these members cannot bear to be pierced,
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	And they do not make him do it except to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the breasts when the milk is thick in the member, to remove the viscosity that is in the body, just as we put leeches on the belly and the buttocks to reduce the body.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an abscess or stone, it removes by its virtue attracting accidentally the abscess, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way, it does when placed on the liver and the spleen when there is retained wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are treated empty to be sucked only; and sometimes they are treated with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in this way the blister is filled with hot water or water in which cooked healing herbs have been steeped.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister to be treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be two fingers' width and half a palm's breadth wide, and have one small hole, as for pushing an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be made of iron, soft before so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a rod of iron or steel, to put a handle on it;
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let them be large or small depending on the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the blisters of children are different from those of the elderly, and thin from thick ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should put this blister on the member thusly:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a beeswax candle or thread, and place it through the blister at the center which is in the blister,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the blister so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then lay it on the member, and your fingers should be above the wound as we have said, so that when one sees, if there is steam, one removes the bladder.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	Then take the linen thread as before and reinforce it often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bladder used in disease of pleurisy, there is no vein or wound, and it is not brought unless when it is full of liquid, and it is placed only on the member.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sanguisettes are not introduced except in members where bandages cannot be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare flesh, like the buttocks or genitals, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and if the quality of the patient is such that when you find sanguisettes in sweet clean waters without purulence, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a new container of sweet water until they are familiar with it and have nothing inside.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then let it be drained of vein and abscess, then rub the member until it turns red and put on plasters.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and hot, if it is possible to apply a leech, do so, for it is very helpful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the affected limb and immerse it in warm water, then wrap it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the healthy limbs become cold due to the plasters, immerse one linen cloth in cold water and place it on until the wound is healed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wound is multiplying, place it on crushed glass or vitriol, and similar things, until it scabs over.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	And you place half-peeled beans on the wound and leave them until they scab over at the site, it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if more help is needed, take other willows.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the willows do not want to be taken, rub the wound with fresh blood or insert a needle until the juice flows out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And then lay them down (the limbs), and as soon as they feel the blood, let them harden.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	When you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle a little aloe vera and lin powder or ashes on it, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures (breaks)
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with setting fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the foolish fool casts himself out of this chapter, who will never see any old books, nor read any letter in them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, science is alienated from our land, because I have never found anyone good at it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else, except through the knowledge of old books, where I have studied extensively to treat the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained within it, and summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are needed, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we explain the summary of this book's content and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	When any break or dislocation, twisting or distortion comes to anyone, you must hasten to heal the patient on both sides, unless anything prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or the elderly.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the time is not too hot or too cold, avoid eating cold foods, such as frosty meat and mutton or veal eyes, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, nor fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you are sure of the abscess heating up, or of the spread of matter to the limb; if the patient follows these primary rules that he has used before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed on foods that cause thick stools, or have viscosity like cooked barley in water and peas, and beef, and pork, and veal, and mutton, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this thick stool, the healing of the fracture is quicker.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and debilitated cannot be well healed or repaired according to their nature due to the relaxation of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But has no cure, reset on the broken bone.i.e. large splints which press and join the limb together, as much as it was before; and do not let him move at all from his work, and for this reason he should be fed with large foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head (skull) is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture which goes towards the elbow, and another in sharpening, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its tool and instrument proper for restoration, according to what memory comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And fractures of the bone are known by this that the joint is twisted and wide open at the end, and it is pressed by the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when it [the dislocation] has no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may have twisting, a fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand at all, but place medicine on it that comes afterwards, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that occur at an angle and are the two separated parts, they must now be made equal again, so that abscesses do not come in.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses become hot, let him leave them for some days, until the abscesses are appeased.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then make it equal to the mouse that you can easily and skillfully catch, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration of one where there are broken bones; then hold it, as is explained hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bones are broken into pieces, divide it into two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or with your hand if it is a small member, or with two strings, or with one string and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the member are disjointed, reset them with all means the additions in their places as you can, and ensure that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And align well the two bones correctly according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that they are not correctly aligned: straighten them nicely, and do not strain or press too much as those who force it out by their work produce abscesses and contractions in the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are set, carefully immobilize the patient so that he does not move, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limbs are so secure that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For if he feels no pain, it is not set correctly, and it must be placed in such a position that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And be aware that it should be put rightly so that deformities do not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken member are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as fingers, thumbs, and similar ones: it is necessary to wrap them in fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and stiff linen, for the broad linen binds the entire large member, and restrains it evenly on all sides, so there is no swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then, tie light bandages around it three or four times according to the member, and hold your hand slightly on the entire length, then go above the fracture and hold it less, than the fracture, then move away from the fracture a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another ligament, and wind it directly over the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the fracture, and hold it moderately, neither too hard nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place dampened linen or cloth strips between the joints until they are all equal, then tie it all together with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is a swelling or abscess, place something soothing for the abscess that is hot and what removes the swelling on top, and leave it in this way for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then fasten your splints, and they should be half the width of a thick stick that is carefully sawed, or a rope from which they make ropes for ships, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the splint that a man places over the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And should also be as long as necessary for the member, whether large or small.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind the splint in the same way you did at the first joint, then sew it on using thread as done at the first fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	The bandage should be closer in this location, rather less so; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	If the threads are thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who make their rope from twisted linen, it is a great error, because the twist cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the limbs of the ribs after setting them in healthy bones, place linen or flax padding beneath them to prevent swelling.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is broken and the nerves are torn, I will tell the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to hold bones of broken members all day long on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For large members, there should not be splints placed except after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: it is that you take flour that is kept in the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant egg, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, on [the affected area], and this is the common method for restoring a fracture using plasters, and this is also suitable for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for healing breaks, dislocations and twists: take albaries, lupine, elm, asafetida and Arabic gum, mix in ten parts; add myrrh and aloes, five parts; seven parts of alkali; then make a powder and mix with yolk of an egg; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition and quickly heals broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for twisting: take mugwort and wormwood, mix in ten parts; add myrrh and aloes, eight parts; six parts of acacia; Armenian pitch ten parts; grind well, and mix with vinegar or yolk of an egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for dislocated joints and swollen bones, and to relieve the pain, they use the bone saw and break it: take new linen, wet in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the place. This plaster does not heal but is good for soothing hot abscesses and proper bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of setting broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth wormwood, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of poultice to heal broken bones and to hasten the healing of an abscess. Take equal parts of mallow root, chamomile, viola flowers, beeswax flour, and grind them together; mix with wine, and if the limbs are scalded, mix with moist coriander water or vinegar, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another stronger method of poultice when the hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take equal parts of mallow root, flax seed, blackthorn, clover, and sassafras; also viola flowers and chamomile flowers; grind them together, and mix with either salt water, sweet water or vinegar, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that no other substance besides a mixture of beeswax and oil should be applied to a broken limb for restoration, and it should neither be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen states that for restoring a broken limb, one should apply warm dry substances such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of application that is useful for wounds and pain: take mugath (possibly a type of plant) and chopped human hair or feathers of birds, and vis amalgam (a substance used in medicine), grind them all together to make a poultice and apply it to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then, dislocate a little after that, and be careful that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not dislocate it by hand for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	If pain, itchiness, lack of rest or swelling occurs at the joint, hasten and dislocate it, and remove the plaster immediately; take a light cloth, sea sponge dampened with water, and immerse in water; lift the joint until the itchiness stops, and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen dampened with water or rose oil on it, and tie it up with a nut until you are sure that the abscess is warm.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then begin the suturing subtly, and a little plaster, and not to strain it too much as before; and suture until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has burst, become red, painful and swollen, and if you need plaster and linen, then suture it as you did before evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If nothing comes to the limb as we have said, do not remove it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the abscess breaks and the incision approaches the skin.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then hold it more tightly than before, and make the flesh thicker, as I said earlier; and if you see the joint drying out more than necessary, know that nutrients cannot enter.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply hot moist heat every time you reset it, and for each three hours, loosen the bandage a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work, then cut the nutrients from the limb, and hasten to correct those who leave the limb twisted: it is harmful, and it is a work of fear; I do not see anything else than labor and working correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	diverse methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	many ways of fractures are, and various shapes, and the causes are determined.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	because there are fractures made by sword strike, and the shaft breaks the entire bone up to the splinter that is under the bone, as when hached or fisted; therefore this type of fracture is called "hachuring".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or the sword strikes the bone from above by piercing it and this type of fracture is called "complete"; and the wound caused by these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a bruise filled with blood, or a wound or arrow wounds, or falling upon a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If it is a swelling that approaches the membrane underneath the bone, or it is on the bone and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is an injury that has penetrated the bone as fine as a hair and it is a small wound, which is called this swelling "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or something similar causes the bone piece to enter within [the wound], and the joints are compressed like the blacksmith does when he hammers on cauldrons; if an arrow enters it.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	This happens more often in those who have moist bones, such as a child's head bone;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And these types of breaks have small fragments dislodged, as I will speak in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breaks by the drawing on them, and the testing inquiry, and through the corruption of flesh that is above. (line-by-line translation)
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of the capillary is known by those who, when the bone is exposed and scraped above, if the break appears black. (line-by-line translation)
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, take care of the patient's circumstances, and if you see any bad accident, as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, stretching, swelling, fever, the hairs coming out and reddening, and other symptoms in various dispositions, it cannot heal with doubt. (line-by-line translation)
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an overwhelming accident, and you hope for salvation, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the splinter first comes to you in winter, it must be removed before the fourteenth day at the bone's mouth.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not rot, and the accidents we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	If the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary to make a cut in the affected area as follows: and take hold of the head of the splintered bone, and remove the covering from the bone on all sides, and above the wound more gently than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood flows to reveal the bone or abscess boils, assist with what is needed and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest until the abscess boils subside, and be assured of the flow of blood; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is called the cutting method.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then insert another, larger incision.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various sizes of blades, some narrow and others wide, sharp and made of iron not copper; and work lightly so as not to pierce the flesh.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and projecting, it is necessary that you pierce around it so that you provide blades with grooves, not sharp enough to penetrate beyond the bone surface, and above the point there should be a margin or circle that prevents the point from passing beyond the bone; and you must have several of them, each coming in its place at the depth of the bone, so that you have grooved blades for all cases; and this is the form of the four types of grooved blades:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place one grooved blade on the bone and turn it with your hand until you feel the bone is pierced; then move the blade to another part a little afterward, and do this all around; then cut the space of the bone between the periosteum, and do this as delicately as possible, lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone or any of the tools you have, such as pliers or forceps; and make sure you do not touch the cerebral membrane or the dura mater.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the tightness that has remained on the bone or another similar instrument resembling an incisor, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	If something remains of the small bones or scales, remove them gently with one instrument; then treat the wound with what we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of work, which is more secretive, is the one that the Greeks call it, and they highly praise it, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture moves open; so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place it under the head of this concave incisor, as shown in the following figure:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and the parts are concave on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, so that you cut lightly around the bone, but take care of the cloth that is underneath:
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it is removed badly with harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the membrane, and the bone is only split from above, and there are small fragments, then after smoothing it, remove the scales with a sharp rasp, having different amounts as necessary, in order to provide the most suitable amount for each place, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with a large rasp, then proceed with finer ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-like or subtle fractures, you must provide a treatment according to its nature; and this is not something that can be answered by one who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, you should take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, wet it in rose oil and place it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another cloth doubled in 2 or 3 layers, wet it in wine and rose oil, place it on the first cloth; do this as lightly as you can, so as not to burden the wound, then administer another string but do not tighten it more than it just covers the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it for 1 day or 2, until the abscess subsides, then remove the string, and provide medicine such as marshmallow root, oats, incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and provide reliable medicines without bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And keep the wound always clean, do not leave any dressing or let it be covered with bandages, for when bandages are placed on the scalp, they rot and cause infection, which brings great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed upon it, it will bite through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then take care, if any harmful event befalls the patient as we have said, it is full of doubtful meaning.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there comes blackness not for any reason other than the medicine that has been applied to it, which may have such power, you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them with one piece of linen cloth and apply it upon it.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the care of methods of treatments, as it is necessary, while he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or only one of them, since they are two bones, but the one below is cartilage and does not break, unless it causes a swelling or deformation, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your little finger or thumb into the nose and align the fracture inside the nostril index, and at the pocket by exhalation, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain due to your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part near the neck and the thumb cannot reach its place, you must align it with the head of a ruler, a little bigger.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	If it is broken in two parts, then do as before, and hasten to restore the first day if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has cooled down, then tie a linen cloth to the neck if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you step on another person or are stepped upon, it breaks [the bone] and the tendons become as thick as they fill the nostrils with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they said some remedy that one should moisten the tendons in butter and boil them each day. It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they be moistened in a concoction of egg white and milled flour; then leave the tendon until the bone is hard, and the cartilages have hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one steps on feathers of goose in place of tendons, and if it is wrapped with a piece of linen, and holds the breakage, and blows warm air [into it]; then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the new (opening) while you are working on it, put either beeswax or cotton wool soaked in rose oil, or a small piece of lignum aloes, there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not come to it (the new opening), apply plaster from without, with flour of sesame, and powder of incense, mixed with egg yolk, then put on light bandages, but do not tie the new opening too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the break in the new opening is small and it breaks into small pieces, then remove with suitable instruments, then close the wound, and treat with things that promote healing such as plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the nose, treat it with cautery and insert sticks of lead until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the break is only displaced and not broken through to the inside, but rather bent within, this can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; if it is on the left side, you should put your index finger of the right hand and push gently into the break, then use the other hand to adjust it from the outside and align it.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is dislocated in two places, then you must administer extension of two parts, equal in size.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If the teeth move or are broken, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a splint on the fractured jaw and put a double cloth over it; put a large and well-made cradle or piece of leather equal to the jaw lengthwise and crosswise, and secure it as you can, and command the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the figure change, dislocate it on the third day and then reset it to its original position; put a poultice on top made with flour or wheat with egg, after removing the splint; put a light linen bandage over the poultice and if the dislocation reoccurs, leave it as long as it is healed; many times it heals in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, bring what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is breakage and wound together, take care that no piece of the bone is removed; use the tools suitable for that purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, you should widen it with fire as necessary.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, close the wound if it is wide, and put on one dressing suitable for that purpose, to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	From the lock (or fastening)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The lock (or fastening) breaks many times in front of the shoulder, and the breakage is in four ways: or it is broken and dislocated in two places, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the break is without wound, that you have two assistants, so one grips the shoulder where the lock feels broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then put the break in equal alignment with your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and has no appearance or bulging.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, put a round cushion of cloth or linen under the patient's shoulder, and let it be thick according to your necessity; stretch and lift the lock, and hold the cushion with your hand, so that you align the break as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out of the joint because it comes in completely, then the patient must lie on their affected side, and a small pillow should be placed under the shoulder, and the attendant should push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find broken bones, then it is necessary that you cut across them; and pull the pieces gently apart, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any obstruction, strike it at one of the incisions you made; but place this instrument under the socket to keep it open.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resemble a spoon, not concave, and be as large as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two handles, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the shape of the wound that you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the abscess's heating, if it opens a wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt about the abscess's heating, then use linen and gauze to cover the wound, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If abscess heating comes, wet linen in rose oil and asafoetida and vinegar, then place on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The bone's compression when it feels wounds and cuts is to put the plaster of milled powder and egg yolk on the bone, place light straws on top, and place a spear underneath if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very long bandage of a palm's width, then put one double cloth damp on top, and roll it up; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the edge of the bandage hangs over.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the chin, and under the patient's chin; and tighten it from each side, and when you see that the fracture aligns properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then reinforce it daily, and when the swelling subsides, hold it in place.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under his chin to lift the shoulder up; align the fracture by moving the shoulder with force or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it except for bad accidents occur, until 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then, if necessary, begin the treatment and hold it steady, and leave it in this state until it is restored; and it is usually restored within 28 days, and sometimes sooner for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is dislocated or broken out of its socket and not moving, it should only be moved by touch; if the injury is apparent, align it according to the nature of the break, and reset it in all ways possible; then put powder from a mill with egg whites and light feathers on it, and cover it with two layers of cloth; then place a large and thin cushion over it, about one finger's width larger than the shoulder, and make sure the cushion is evenly spread under every part of the shoulder, so that the feathers fill the gap between the cushion and the shoulder equally; and then bind it tightly with a great bandage to prevent the cushion from moving from its place, and observe the patient daily; whenever the pain subsides, reset the shoulder if necessary, and keep the feathers evenly placed on the cushion; lay the patient on his side; and the shoulder will be restored within 20 or 30 days. And when this number is reached, unbind it, and be careful because it is not bone that becomes loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front and not below the skin, lift it up, remove the bone, and do as we have said in the fracture of the fistula to treat an abscess by heating.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the fistula
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The piece is sometimes broken in the middle, but it happens rarely; however, it often breaks off at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, it sinks down below, causing the patient great pain, and without a splint, and quickly, and possibly vomiting blood, and the channels open in the broken bone, and he feels everything very badly.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back with their head down, and one cushion is placed between the shoulders, then the shoulders are pressed and the ribs are brought together to your hands, and it must be done carefully so that the bone figure is as required; then salt poultice and bandages are put on top of the broken bone, or a light cloth, and it is wrapped in one cloth, and it is tied to the broken bone so that it does not move; and you turn the limb roundabout, and tighten it gradually, and check each hour if it heals, and if it softens, tighten again; and if it needs to be dislocated due to corrosion or inflammation at the location, or pain or abscess, hurry up, and dislocate it, remove the poultice, and address those who came with ways of treatment; then reattach the poultice, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of a broken rib
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs occurs only in large ones behind the back and in the chest, and they do not break easily except due to moisture; and it is well felt at the inquiry with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restorations are such that you must set the break evenly, as required. Then place the splint, and apply a steady pressure if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break in the ribs is sinking inside, the patient feels intense pain and shortness of breath, similar to pleurisy, for the bone punctures the lining; and the edges are sharp, and immediately he vomits a large amount of blood, which is serious illness, and the ancients have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the break outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot poultices come, unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have arrived, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that someone should put leeches on the wound to drain pus, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the leech does not attract excess fluid to the wound due to its weak constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that someone should cover the wound with damp linen soaked in hot oil and put bandages between the ribs to even out the swelling around it; then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear through the bone which does not pierce the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, it is necessary to cut above the broken rib, and it is necessary to put one instrument underneath for support; then you must saw the bone, pull it gently, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat with plasters until it is healed. And if an abscess comes, place damp cloths soaked in rose oil on it, and put it there; and heal the rib while it is necessary to do so, and lie down with it resting where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes the bones in the neck break and do not bend; and similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, take notice if their hands are softened, swollen and dead, and cannot be moved or stretched, and when you prick them with a needle, they feel nothing. Know that they are mortally wounded in many positions, but if they do not move and feel when they are pressed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
