Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when this happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if it will be healed or not, take notice if the feet are softened, and if there is a swelling that is in the hands, and the back suddenly jumps with spasm and discharge involuntarily; and when it is pressed on the belly, it jumps involuntarily. And when it is pressed on the back and he wishes to straighten himself, he cannot. Know that it is mortally wounded: do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this incident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you anoint [the abscess] with rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters and tie it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the part where they feel pain, until it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, it should be covered [with something]; then remove the bone, join the two edges of the wound with stitches if it is large, and treat the wound with healing salve until it heals; and if the head of the bone (which is called "the heads of the cow") is broken, take your left hand, put it on the dislocated part and hold it equal to your right hand, then apply the plaster and the linen bandage, if you have them; then tighten [the bandage], and if there are bones protruding, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ankle bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it occurs, there is only a little lessening of the pain at the site; and it extends along the length, bends towards the crotch, causes pain and swelling at the site that breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the healing is that you extend your hand above [the break], so that you are over the break; and recognize where the break is and what its shape is; and if the break is only at the top, then set the break equal to its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is along the length or it bends inward, make the patient lie on his stomach so that the healing of the break comes to your attention.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it (the dislocation) right, put an armature on it, then put a splint of wood or horn over it and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the lever below the ribs until the patient is comfortable.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess comes to the surface, do not touch it until the abscess has calmed down, and place what we have previously mentioned on it; then return to treatment, and hold it as necessary, if there is no bad occurrence; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is the part that is between the neck and the arm, and if it is fractured, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: of which one is that you take a rod filled with coarse material, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the rod to each other and raise them up, and place the patient on one seat; then drop the broken arm onto the rod, until it reaches the level, and have a hump in the rod, then raise something heavy above it or the assistants extend it downwards; then place the hands of the molder on the fracture equally, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that you lay the patient on his bed, tie one end of the rod to his neck and command two assistants that one holds the part above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds both ends of the rod, each pulling in their respective directions.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then hold one ligament beneath the break, and above the break, and extend each of the assistants to their part. And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, then you must put a moderate ligament beneath the joint, and another towards the flesh, beneath the break; and in the same way if the break is towards the flesh, you must put a light ligament without labor, until the break is equal on the joint, and on the flesh; then make it equal, as necessary, and hold it, unless an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess does come, do not hold it for more than seven days, and put a soft cloth in oil of roses on it to soothe the abscess; then hold it, and the method of holding it is that you place the plaster on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and put the towel, and hold it onto the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in its correct position, unless anything prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone is moving, use wedges, and put a larger and stronger wedge on the break than the others, and have one space between each wedge, and let each wedge be so large that it passes the break two fingers width from each side; then hold onto the wedges, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, with more force but less in pulling away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the abscess of the arrowhead, and the constriction, as we have said, during the time that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is cold, leave it to heal until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every third day at the suture, to see if pus does not swell or appear at the site, or the inflammation does not come to the limb because it is too narrow. If this happens, proceed as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If such accidents do not occur, the arrow should not be removed before three or more days, and the patient should lie on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place an equal linen cushion under the arrowhead and watch every hour of the day or night that the limb does not move or the suture is not loose; proceed by the power of medicine and give the food as we have previously stated, so that the food is initially fine; when it starts to recover, let it be coarse. It is customary for the arrow and the thigh to be re-inserted within forty days; then remove and administer baths and ointments for the wound to heal. If the constriction is ugly and swollen, wait longer to remove it, up to one month.
de la brisure du bras	on the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones, which are called the "two shafts"; one is small, and it is the one that forms the elbow; the other is large, and it is the one below, near the little finger; sometimes only the large shaft breaks, or sometimes both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small shaft breaks, the restoration and healing are easy; but when the large one breaks, healing is poor and more difficult than when both break together. If it's only the small shaft that breaks, you should slightly extend it gently and straighten it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large shaft that breaks, you should apply more force; extend it up to one cubit, lift the elbow of the hand higher than the others, and the smaller finger lower than the others, cross the patient over himself, and place a cubit above him, so that the patient does not feel any discomfort; then stretch out the ministers' arms below their hand, or to the elbow, and have one minister on one side and another on the other above. Then align the broken bone according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no dislocation that pricks the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut off and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If with the break at the joint, I have spoken of it in the individual chapter; then take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	If in the beginning of the setting it occurs that abscesses appear, apply one linen cloth made of rose oil and white wax, not too hard nor too soft; and lay one cloth carefully over the abscesses, so that they are pacified. Then remove the wax, and place a plaster with milled powder and egg white; then put in sticks (splints), and make the stick of the breakage stronger and a little wider than the others; and know that it should have 7 splints or more in various positions: whether the breakage is in one bone or two; and hold the breakage more at the top, and less on the sides, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are over the breakage be soft and moist, not too hard nor rough; and let the thread, with which it is tied, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And examine the member and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents occur in the member, such as itching that occurs in the member, then you must irrigate the member with hot water until the itching is relieved; and let the member not rest. Then repeat the treatment, and if the ligaments are damaged and the bones dislocated, or similar things, give the advice accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the urine cannot reach the member due to it being too narrow, then you must soften it with oil for a few days, until the urine passes through, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things mentioned above occur in the patient, then do not release him until 20 days or more. Inquire about his hands to his neck, and make sure his neck is even, and watch for movement and tilting, and let him sleep on his back; know that this break will be healed in 30 or 40 days, or perhaps in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	For at the back of the hand and the fingers, there are few fractures, but it occurs repeatedly many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is fractured or dislocated, the patient should lie flat on his back, with arms straight and evenly aligned; then he places his hand on a stretched cloth, and the attendant extends the broken bones and aligns them as much as possible; then apply plaster and compresses, if abscess does not occur; then apply a splint according to the severity of the fracture; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the side of the sole near the abdomen, make a splint from cloths, and instruct the patient to press his injured hand against it; then bind it with a long piece of cloth, and the splint should be as large as the palm of the hand, and tightened as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the edge, you must place a splint above and another beneath in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand and stop the flow of blood between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the break comes on any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, equalize it as necessary; hold it with the sole and, if you see that it is displaced, place a straight splint to lift the break and immobilize it; if the break is in the other fingers (such as the index or another), equalize them and tie them with the healthy finger that follows; tie all of them in one binding, which is enough, or place a splint, such as a thumb-splint; take care in restoring and positioning the abscess, and apply heat to it as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the leg are often broken, and one sees it when it twists forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one ties a ligament above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patients lie on their face, then each attendant extends their ligament equally to its part; and this is when the break is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If the break is near the root of the leg, one ligament should be towards the heel and the others towards the break. And similarly, if it is near the knee, then extend the ligaments on the outside of the knee, and the extension below; then place the bones equally in their two hands, as they are by nature, and then apply the splint, and bind it, without an abscess coming.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that heats up, let it cool down first, then return to your work and treatment; the ligature is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must bind over the fracture. That is to say, bind a strong bandage of doubled linen and let the superfluous parts protrude, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the knee, and insert one long thread between the thigh and the leg, under the knee, and bring the end of the thread to the top; then turn both the leg and the thigh over the bandage, then put two bars on the break, and put a bar on the bone of the leg; then use soft cloth between the leg and the thigh to equalize the binding, then start tying four twists or six on the fracture; and as you go higher on the fracture, loosen it; then hold the two threads that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, bind three bars on top, then return to the bottom of the thread until you come across the foot; tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it as it is, and let there be no sign of abscess or swelling nor anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a break, straighten it as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they must be cut off if possible; and if it cannot be done, the limb must be broken and the bone removed; and cure it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken so that it can be splinted like in the shoulder or arm; however, in this kind of restoration, the patient does not feel pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored within a few days, either less or more, according to the various complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the street of the knee, there is little fracture, but it often bends. And if it breaks, it is not a complete break, only a crack or a fissure, and it causes pain everywhere and without a specific location, and this is felt very much.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes the bone that is broken at its ends, as long as it can be assembled; then put the splint, and place a round peg there if needed, and tighten it as required, then recheck all the arrangements mentioned in other breaks, such as an abscess, boil or similar; for each accident, use what is required until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "shin" and the others are called "fibula"; and it has all the same breakages as in the arm, and therefore the restoration is equal to that of the arm, and the work is entirely the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; and it turns underneath. Then bring extension, make it even, and tie the edges equally; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly and there are many pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; and align according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two fists full of splints that support the leg on both sides and are as long as the length of the leg from the knee to below; then wrap them in two layers, one above and one below, and tie them at this point, and the leg will not be able to decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should provide a splint as long as the leg, and it should be of wood, and they place the leg on it to prevent movement, and properly make this in the fracture where there is pain; and move the leg every day to see if there is any abscess or other accident; and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but there may be fracture of the bones in the foot and toes, and it has no cure except for compression in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones in the foot, and you see these bones protruding one above the other, place the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wants to walk, then place your foot under his, where the bones are raised, and press them back into their places; then apply the splint and padding, and put a small table under the foot with two flat surfaces, then tighten it around the foot in the appropriate way; once you have wrapped the cloths around it, and other things that you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the splint, because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [bones] are broken, restore them as we have said in the hand bones; then place a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and it should be slightly larger; then place a wooden block beneath the fractured one, as I have said, and hold it aligned; and if there are two or more, or more, break each bone separately, place a splint over each one according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the wooden block under the fracture; and ensure that the head of the block is facing the abdomen of the limb, so it covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have said; and treat each accident as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the womb is broken by natural childbirth, make her sit with her legs apart, then lean her towards the part of the back and hold her from behind; then fill the cavity of nature with cotton and also put as much as a stone in it; then turn the woman, lift up her buttocks little by little, and the cotton will burst out to the entrance of the nature, and the bone will return with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of straw, tie one end of a cord to it, and push the whole bladder into the nature; then blow forcefully into the cord until the bladder is inflated inside: the fracture will return; then fill with cotton and leave it for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the arm is broken in man or woman, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures should not be concealed from him who puts his study and practice to them and attends my book. For the fracture indicates in many ways the right way of restoration: take note of that then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and insert the penis; then wrap it in cloth and leave it for 3 days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	with break (or fracture) and wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For that person who has a fracture with a wound (or break with wound), especially if it is large as the leg bone or shoulder blade or similar, it should be cauterized now, as the cauteries that we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, it should be sealed with vitriol (a disinfectant), if you have no other option, then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour, or on that day, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess bursts, allow the healing to continue until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is appeased; do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks open in the hollow of the cavity, you must set it gently and slightly extend it.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not aligned for you to set it evenly in your hands, you will need this tool made of iron that has 7 or 8 inches long and its width according to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the mirror that he holds .3 or 4, depending on what is needed in each cure of breaking bones; and it should be round and slightly larger than a coin so it does not bend under compression on the member during your work, and sharp before, and thick from the middle to the tip, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", because the crooked neck should be placed on top of the obvious bone; push it once until it returns, and make it even on both sides. If the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then you must cut the apparent bone, so that the instruments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot return the bone as we have said, if you have an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, use it to your power; then gnaw that which is left in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position. Do as much as you can to get it in its place, then moisten one linen cloth in black stiptic wine, or if it's in summer, moisten the cloth in water; do not put any oil-soaked cloth or anything over the wound that could cause corruption and putrefaction; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cover the dressing all around, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times have foolish surgeons done this, causing death or corruption of the patient sometimes; and let the bandages be softer and more pliable than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad incident will come about, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, do not put splints on it; but wrap around instead, in place of splints, hard bandages and bind them. And when after one day or two you see pus boiling at the wound, remove completely what you had placed on top, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be prepared in such a way that the splints slide downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they pass many days without healing and continue to swell again, know that there are small bone fragments; therefore, you must carefully open the wound and remove all the dislocated fragments causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If a fistula or corruption comes to the place, you must treat it according to what is said in the chapter before this one. And when the bone is broken and opened above the limb, such as the bone of the shin or shoulder, and similar large bones, do not draw it out; for many times death may come, but leave it until it can heal by itself; perhaps a charrion cart will be needed after twenty or thirty days. Then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	broken bones that come on the suture (joint)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after health following the break, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a pitiful sight to see the shape of the limb; and unfortunately, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take good care of it afterwards: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and saracocola, acacia, and similar others, taking any one of these substances or all together and boil them in a stiptic wine or with an abundance of egg or with oil; then place the mixture in a bandage and apply pressure and do not remove it for many days; then dislocate it, and start another, until the nodulation is removed; or you hold above a piece of wood well made; for the properties of wood are that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, chop it off, and make the excess apparent; or you shave it at any razor until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb that is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is set and remains afterwards, the limbs become weak and delicate; this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nutrients could not reach the member; or due to excessive swelling; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body strong, until the flesh multiplies in him; then provide baths, and give him joy and rest; next apply salve to the member, so that the salve attracts great nutrients, and often apply cold water to it, until the nutrients reach the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the limb is disfigured, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish who say that one should break the limb anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and this practice is condemned, and it causes great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the knots and tortures are fresh, they must be softened with hot water or softening herbs such as vismalve leaves, root radishes, sweet clovers, and similar things; and you should make a soothing plaster using dyaquilon well-made, and take musk from vismalve, mix it with gelyn grease or sesame oil, and apply the plaster; or you can take greased figs, grind them with corn bran, and similar medicines that alleviate pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the knots are removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands. Movement should be introduced to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortures are hardened and strengthened like stone, requiring surgery, it must be covered up to the bone, at the subtle incision; and cotton and wool should be placed in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	If dislocation occurs in anyone, it must now be repositioned with care.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if it is delayed, the limb swells, and in case it is placed back at its joint; therefore, it should not be moved before it is swollen: many times this causes pus and other pain.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Throughout, when this happens, you sanitize the patient, then let him be, until all abscesses are appeased; then moisten the limb with hot water and oil, then gently move it, and care for each member as care comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	of jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	1. Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous: It happens that the jaws are dislocated in two ways: either they are partly dislocated from their place and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards down, causing saliva to flow from the mouth which it cannot hold, and it cannot close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return in various positions more often.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and finished, you must reset it quickly, without hesitation;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a manner that the minister holds the patient's head and pushes the thumb of one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is from two parts; and the other hand should be open, to make it even; and instruct the patient to soften and move their jaws from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And bring the thumb equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reset is difficult, similarly, if it is both jaws together, apply hot water and oil to loosen them gently; do not rush to forcefully move, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they (dislocations) are set back in place equally, and the mouth of the patient is closed well, cover it with a cloth moistened with rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with several strips.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on his back, and his arms be placed between two pillows, so that it does not move to the right or left, nor force itself at all, but take light meat, until the pain is gone, and the jaws are tied.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat lightly whatever he wants, and not to work at all in opening the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaws are well tied and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset in an hour and are not returned to their place, fever and usual sweats occur, and perhaps abdominal swelling, and possibly vomiting bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see this, therefore, know that it is disaster; and many times the one in whom it occurs dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the collarbone   (metaphorical usage, meaning "neck" or "throat")
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The splint cannot dislocate from the side within the ribcage and is dislocated outside once at the hip, and it is felt clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then presses the joint with your palm and it will return; then put a splint and bandage over it and hold it in place.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the joint that is toward the back cannot dislocate; if it does, then reset it to its place as we have said; then put a splint and bandage over it and hold it in place, and instruct the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And likewise, bring back the head of the spine when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in four ways: one of which is when it dislocates at the part near the shoulder joint below; and the second way is to the part of the buttock; and by chance it may dislocate above, but this rarely happens.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And never dislocate backwards for the shoulder, and never dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocate downwards towards the axilla, especially in those who have little flesh, for it leaps out quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it leaps out slightly, and returns slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes happens to some men percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must verify it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocations occur when they move downwards towards the shoulder, and you should distinguish between a diseased shoulder and a healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	You will find a hollow in the shoulder blade and beneath the shoulder to the touch of the shoulder head, just as there is an eye socket; and the patient cannot return their hand to its place, nor make any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And if it is dislocated upwards, it will not be hidden, for you can feel it clearly by touching.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this method of dislocation is not always easy to reset, when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The minister lifts the patient's hand high, then puts your fist underneath it, and pulls the joint up forcefully to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and stretches it high, then puts it underneath; quickly it will come back.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said within a few hours, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and they should be given a soothing and calming balm, such as a decoction of elderflower and fenugreek in water, and it should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the patient should lie down on their back and place a piece of even linen under the affected shoulder, neither too soft nor too hard, then the healer places his foot on the cloth and gently lifts the head of the shoulder, pulling the arm of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another assistant holds the head of the patient still below it; that shoulder will return immediately. If you see it dislocate again in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and have one man who is larger than the patient be present. He should be positioned straight alongside the cost side, and push the shoulder of the patient down under his own, lifting the affected shoulder upward so that the patient hangs in an "A" shape.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister pulls the hand of the patient towards the abdomen. If the patient is too weak, he can hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is also pulled in another way: and that one drives a long needle into the ground so that the head is as round as a pea, but neither too large nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then it should be placed under the patient, but with soft wool beneath, and the patient should be lying along the length of the bed; then his hand on the affected side should be extended towards the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not want to return due to all these things that we have said, perform this treatment: take one stick of two hands in length and four fingers in width, which has its head round for easy insertion deep inside the anus, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie the head of the stick with cloth to prevent the patient from being scalded, then insert the stick into the anus of the patient; extend one arm along the stick, and bind the shoulder to the stick, and the forearm at the end of the hand, then place one leg on one side of a bench, and let the other side hang loose; the dislocation will be reduced immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is inside, no matter how, you must put a sphere of cotton equal in size under the anus, then place a plaster filled with powder from the mill, along with incense and egg yolk, all over the shoulder and around; then hold it down beneath the anus, turn the string around the plaster, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little food, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is hardened and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has come or for another reason, then you must administer three cauterizations as stated in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you have done all of this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve to the shoulder is cut or stretched out or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the hip and limbs, front or back, is caused by force and extension of hands, and other means are administered for its treatment; it should be cured until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing, if there is still pain in the limb and slow movement, the patient should use baths several times until the pain subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost   (This line seems incomplete, as it does not seem to follow the pattern of translation from the previous lines.)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the arm is dislocated at points, and it comes back at points; and if it becomes dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repaired because it can be seen clearly and felt clearly; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the sick arm with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly. For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset the dislocation in such a way that the abscesses come out easily, for if the abscess comes out, it would be difficult to set; and perhaps it cannot be set completely from all sides, especially when it is at the back; it is worth more than other dislocations, and it causes greater pain, and perhaps death follows.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows, when it can be returned to its state, extend your hand to both of his hands; and stretch out his arms, and place his hands opposite each other according to the bone joints outside and inside, and push the joint back to its sockets or to the root of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when you fold your hand over your other hand, and push against the bone joint that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is necessary for two people to extend the arm, and one person should hold it still during the extension; then turn the arm from both sides, and when you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the master joins the joint to his hand, he applies some oil to soften the joint, then pushes the joint back into place until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in place, he puts on a plaster made with egg white and applies pressure to form it, then straps the arm around the patient's neck for several days, then unstraps it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is held in place, you unbind it and leave it. If you see that the joint is not holding well, you repeat the plaster and binding, and leave it like that for some days until it is firmly set; then you unbind it again.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels pain after the repositioning of the joint, and it becomes motionless, then bathe it well and rub it, and press until it is soothed; or you place a sheep's grease nail on the jointure, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make it enter the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	and when it swells, rub the jointure gently, then place the nail back on, and then enter into the bath; and do so two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see, place warm dampened wool with butter on it, and strap it; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand joint, and its reset is easy, more than other jointures, nonetheless it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour when it is dislocated, before the joint is swollen or there comes an abscess hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the repositioning is that you put the diseased hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and mirror the hand so it aligns, with its palm above the appearance of the jointure, and push it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Furthermore, you must watch to see if it is in its place; then make the patient lay the back of his hand on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, the patient should place the back of their hand on the table, and the one who is helping should place their hand above the affected joint area. If it returns to its place now, that's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	And if not, strain with plasters or soothing poultices the abscesses and let them remain in place to start healing.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	If it cannot tolerate that, and you cannot put it back in place after any days, the dislocated joint will remain displaced.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And it is not advisable for the patient to be forced to move his hand until the hand is healed, and cannot grasp anything entirely: therefore know that the nerves are severed or the arteries; there is no other remedy but to force by fire cautery in this case, and by chance, nothing else has value.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at its place, put a splint on it as we have said, then bind and leave for 5 days, then unbind and leave in this manner.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot be moved well and there is no pain, moist with warm water and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers on the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	The fingers on the hand are sometimes dislocated on one side or the other, sometimes at the back of the palm or the palm itself;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then push the finger back into its place, and hold the head of the finger while you bend it toward the part where it is dislocated;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and leave it for two days, and then make it straight on the third day; bind it tightly, as we have said, and loosen it by a day, and move it, and tie it again; do this often until it is straight;
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And similarly (do) the same, if it is dislocated from the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and similarly do when it is dislocated from another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	And for the dislocation of the small of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the small of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are many such dislocations without a cure, death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the excretions jump involuntarily, and they cannot be held; many times, any member is softened, either both legs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the spine is affected in four parts; that which affects the rear part is called "gibbosities":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The cure is that you check if the gibbosities have come from childhood; if there is no treatment or healing from it entirely.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, the ancient ways of cure used to speak in great words, but it is not profitable in all cases.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the case of the illness that precedes, there is no remedy nor healing;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and similarly that which comes straight in two sides, can only be cured by the one coming from behind, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that the patient should be extended on an even surface, and have restraint beneath him, so he does not bleed.
