puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then insert one poker into the head on the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a cord under the patient's buttocks, and another at the thighs, and at the knees, and at the ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two ministers know the cords, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two pokers.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let them be tightly closed, the torches as we have said, and the hands place their palms on the spine, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, take a table 3 feet long and rounded on the top, and place the patient on their side. Then push the edge of the table underneath the opening and place the middle part of the table on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And the attendant places their feet on the other end of the table and presses hard until it returns to its place; if you see that it does not return, you do it with the tournet that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you insert two needles into the patient's head from one arm and two others in the feet, and there should be a palm's space between each needle.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and there should be one suture in each needle, or turn the needle, and the needles should be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between two needles there should be one moving needle, as with a thread, and in two moving needles there should be two small needles of a palm's length for turning the needle.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the thread that is among the needles to the needle in the head, and the other thread to the needle at the feet, and each of the ministers turns the needle along the whole length, and the master sets the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is equalized (the dislocated joint), place a dry plaster with egg white on top, then press and then apply an iron rod of three feet long, which penetrates the swelling and the healthy part of the vertebrae, then tie it with a cord as we have said, and use gentle massage until it is healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	if anything comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the rod as we have said before; and sometimes they administer a piece of wood.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and sometimes the appearance comes at the back of the spine, and it is thought to be dislocation; but it is the bone that opens, so one should not have presumption: by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the shoulder and the arm joints come out of place only by dislocations themselves, not otherwise as with other joints; and the shoulder joint is dislocated in four ways: inside and outside, front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when the injured leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the injured knee joint is wider than the healthy, and the injured person cannot bend their knee in fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the loin that is dislocated inflamed with abscess, because the knee joint comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that one who suffers from this condition is that this event happens contrary to what was mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that one whose leg is swollen as mentioned before, are that it is not doubled in the knee, and does not feel pain when bent, and if you wish to make it walk, it cannot move forward, and holds back its urine, and the ankle inflates, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that one whose condition is at the back, are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it double, and this leg is twisted more than the other, and the ankle becomes softened, and the head of the thighbone is beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this similarity of dislocation are such that you should observe if the dislocations are old and remain in their position without any treatment; and it is not appropriate for there to be any assumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	For one whose dislocation is recent, and there are four types of dislocation, you should hurry that you turn the joint, push it inward and outward, and move it left and right; by chance if it returns, no further treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you should prepare one strong attendant and hold the leg firmly with two hands or tie one rope above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another minister extends his hand over it in such a manner that he pushes his hands beneath the buttocks, then tightens a rope-like thing on the thigh; and another grips the head of the thigh with the rope.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And they all extend from above and below at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If the shoulder is not dislocated, a cure for its condition should be applied. When the dislocation is at the front, you must hold the patient on their healthy side, then put the rope around the root of the thigh, and the limb that is underneath the angle, then pull the rope upward towards the angle, and towards the shoulder.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another minister and grasp the large limb of the sick thigh and extend it outward in this manner: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then you must tie the feet of the patient together with a strong rope above the heels and knees, and the sick leg should be extended two feet more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then it should be hung from a post by the neck, and there should be two long arms below; then command one minister to embrace the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient who will embrace the thigh, as the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is on the outside, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has gout, and draw a string over the diseased leg properly, and also over the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then insert two needles, one at the head and one at the feet, then stick one needle between the thighs of the patient in this manner;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And let it be planted with moist cloths around it, so that it does not hurt the patient; then each minister should approach him and place his hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that is good. If not, place it on a table and press as we have said in the previous section, and make the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be straightened quickly, as I have said; and place the hand on the opposite side of the injured angle, then press with the other hand and pull towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back (of the body), it should not be extended downward, nor raised up on earth, but rather it should be as when a hunchback is dislocated at the back, as we have said in the laying of two hunchbacks.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and it (the affected limb) should be on its face, and the ligament extended as we have said before, and it must be pressed strongly against the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it (the affected limb) will be ready when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, place a support (or brace), and bind it with a bandage, so that the hunchback does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And it rests for 3 or 4 days, then dislocate, place a splint on it; and if they are even, hold steady as before, and let them be. For 3 days; then dislocate, and make it move well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation in the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: inside and out, backward; and never forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his thigh with both hands and pull it back between your hands, then bend the two sides of the thigh into a shape; and another minister extends his foot until the thigh returns to its place, and the signs are that it bends easily at the knee.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And apply the plaster on top, and bind the leg to the thigh tightly for three or four days, then dislocate it; and let the patient not walk at all until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it heals.
de la dislocation dou talon	about the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the symptoms are that the ankle is swollen, and tenderness in the area where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the relocations are light, and it should be gently extended to the hands when only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, you must make the patient sit straight, and hold one minister (assistant) by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then lift it up and push the foot upwards strongly;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice as we said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, continue the work, because it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this way, place the patient on his back on the ground, and make a firm hole in the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around it so that the patient does not bleed;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then anoint the ministers the thigh, and another minister extends the leg at the hands or at one joint, so that it lies across the neck of the leg;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then each minister extends equally, and the passer-by should be close between the patient's thighs to hold the patient while stretching him;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then the master puts both hands on the dislocation and another minister anoints the healthy leg below it, and the dislocation will return quickly;
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at the point, apply the plaster and bandage on top, press firmly, bind the leg to the foot, and watch the nerves that are above the back of the calf, so that the binding is not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then let it rest for 2 or 3 days, and if the ligaments soften, hold them tight; then release it on the third day or the fourth, and prevent the patient from walking for 4 days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he goes before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess swells up, you must calm it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	of the two [shoulders]
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both shoulders are dislocated, they must be carefully stretched out without strain, and it is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any way near the back of the hip, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or table straight up, and place your foot over the affected joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns to its place.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is even and there is no opening, place a two-legged table under the foot, press firmly on it, and leave it for four hours, then release it; let it rest until it heals.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When wound comes with the dislocation, and it is to be restored, many times patients die.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	Do not be hasty in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and slow, do not be bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and apply at the beginning of soothing abscesses warmly, and leave the patient in the hands of God if you see no hope for health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, reset the limb to its place, thus allowing the abscess to heal;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	When the limb is in place, administer remedies to calm the abscess and treat the wound as necessary, using dry poultices.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	If there is a dislocation with a fracture and small bones are displaced, set the bones and perform what has been said for simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And guard against entering into fear, as I have said, for it avails you according to your Creator, and by the skill of your weapon and body. Amen
Explicit le romen de fisique	This is the end of the medical text.
